▲The Arrest of a Fraudulent Agent for a Detective Position: A man surnamed Hu, named Shen Yu, who lives in Cang Lane and once worked as a reporter stationed in Zhenjiang for a Shanghai tabloid, was previously driven out of the area for specializing in spreading rumors and swindling. Having no way to make a living, Hu went to Shanghai and disappeared for a long time. Recently, Hu secretly returned to Zhenjiang and was seized by a man named Yin Guangcai yesterday morning and taken to the Second Branch Bureau. According to Yin, six months ago, Hu claimed to be working for the Water Police Team and promised to help him obtain a detective position, demanding a fee of 240 yuan, of which 80 yuan had been paid. However, six months had passed, the matter was never completed, and Hu had disappeared. Today, they met on the road, so he seized him and brought him to the bureau for investigation. After a preliminary hearing by the branch chief, Hu admitted to promising Yin a job but claimed to have only taken 27 yuan for entertainment expenses, with the rest of the money being used by Yin himself for socializing. When asked about his profession, he claimed to be working for the Shanghai police force. Branch Chief Zhang believed that the case involved fraud and obtaining money and immediately prepared a document for transfer to the General Bureau, so that it could be transferred to the court for interrogation.

Gaoyou 110

▲The Chelou Ear Gate Has Been Opened: The New Three Dam Construction Office of the Southern Chelou Project previously blocked the Chelou Ear Gate to construct the tongue under the Chelou Dam. Now, due to the drought and the river water drying up, the rice fields urgently need irrigation. Therefore, farmers in the Second District all appealed to the District Office, requesting relief to prevent the rice fields from withering. Afterwards, District Chief Zhang Shiyan submitted a request to Wang Shuxiang, the director of the dam management, to quickly open the Chelou Ear Gate to save the crops. Director Wang commissioned Engineer Chen to investigate. The day before yesterday, District Chief Zhang, along with Zhang Eryou, the secretary-general of the Wuche Township Farmers Association, and Zhang Zhenbang, a resident of the district, went to visit Director Chen and negotiated for an early opening. Director Chen approved the request. It is now heard that the gate was opened yesterday (the 11th).

Hangzhou 111

▲The Liangzhe Salt Administration Will Be Abolished: Zhou Junyan, the Liangzhe Salt Transport Commissioner, who concurrently served as the director of the Zhejiang Provincial Finance Department, has held this position for six years. Now, the Central Salt Affairs Administration has been taken over by the Chief of the Audit Office, who also serves concurrently. Zhou received a telegram from the Ministry of Finance today, stating that in order to save expenses and unify authority, he was instructed to immediately close the Salt Transport Commissioner's Office and transfer all salt affairs administrative matters to Feng Ruliang, the Chief of the Liangzhe Salt Affairs Audit Branch Office in Hangzhou, who will serve concurrently. Zhou was originally scheduled to go to Shanghai today to negotiate a loan but was unable to do so due to this development. He is now instructing the three sections of the administration—General Affairs, Sales, and Audit—to begin closing the office. According to Zhou, the administration was originally only responsible for salt affairs administrative matters, while salt tax revenue was collected entirely by the Salt Audit Branch Office, so closing the office will be easy and can be completed within days. The approximately 100 employees of the administration and the salt affairs administration will be taken over by the Audit Branch Office, which will inevitably lead to a major reduction in personnel. Whether the dozen or so salt fields in various counties of the province will be merged into local salt affairs audit branches or weighing and distribution bureaus is another matter. However, according to what the reporter knows, the salt tax has long been used to repay foreign debts, so each audit office has a deputy chief, who is a foreigner, to supervise the salt affairs and finances. This time, the Audit Office will take over the administration's affairs, which is a preliminary step towards implementing the merger.

Important News

5th Day Chronicle: Chemistry Conference 112

General Assembly Passed Various Resolutions Yesterday

Nanjing, 5th: The Ministry of Education Chemistry Conference opened its general assembly at 8:00 AM on the 5th, with 40 members attending and Chen Kezhong presiding. The chairmen of each sub-group reported on the resolutions of their respective groups. First, the Curriculum Standards and Translation Group presented its report on the review of curriculum standards for junior high school, senior high school, and university. After discussion and amendment, it was passed. In addition, an additional report on six curriculum standards proposals and a translation review proposal and its attachments were discussed and passed. Next, the National Defense Chemistry Group reported on the group's resolutions, which were amended and passed. Among them, regarding researchers, there were proposals to request the Ministry of Education to establish a national defense professorship and to request all universities and academic institutions to establish national defense chemistry professorships and national defense chemistry research laboratories within their capabilities. Regarding education and propaganda, there were proposals to request the National Compilation and Translation Bureau to compile and translate national defense chemistry books for widespread dissemination and to request the Ministry of Education to broadly disseminate national defense chemistry knowledge to the public. There were three proposals regarding organizational industries, etc. Regarding other matters, there were proposals to request the government to exempt agricultural and industrial salt and domestically produced industrial alcohol from taxes and to abolish the monopoly on saltpeter and sulfur. The chairman proposed that the graduates of the Chemical Engineering Department of National Central University requested assistance from the conference to restore the Chemical Engineering Department of the school. All members said that they personally expressed sympathy, but the general assembly was inconvenient to discuss. Subsequently, the representatives of the General Staff explained that the department welcomed

the members of the conference to come for discussions. The members unanimously agreed. Afterwards, members such as Wang Jiliang proposed to request the Ministry of Education to convey to the government on behalf of the members attending this chemistry conference their willingness to participate in national defense chemistry work to fulfill their national responsibilities. The meeting passed the resolution and immediately elected Huang Xinyan, Chen Yuguang, Zeng Zhaolun, Hu Ankai, and Ding Sixian as representatives to go to various government agencies after the meeting on the 6th to present their opinions and discuss the various proposals, hoping that they would be adopted and implemented. The meeting adjourned at 1:00 PM.

5th Day Chronicle: Conference on Curriculum Standards for Primary and Secondary Schools 113

▲Prescribing Objectives for Civic Training and Self-Study Hours for All High Schools

Conference Concludes, Curriculum Standards to Be Consolidated and Submitted to the Ministry of Education for Promulgation

Nanjing, 5th: The primary and secondary school curriculum conference, the primary school group's general assembly started at 8:00 AM on the 5th, and the secondary school group's afternoon general assembly started and adjourned at 8:00 PM. The two groups' meetings concluded simultaneously, and all members left Nanjing in different directions that evening. It was resolved that the curriculum standards would be handed over to the standing committee for consolidation and then submitted to the Ministry of Education for promulgation.

(1) Primary School Group 114

The Primary School Group Resolved:

(1) Operational Requirements for Civic Training are divided into four categories: morality, recreation, politics, and economics.

(2) The General Outline of the Primary School Curriculum is to be arranged by the standing committee. (3) The Overall Objectives of Primary School Education remain in accordance with the original proposal. (4) A table should be included in the general outline, implementation standards, and implementation measures to indicate the textbook issues for each subject.

(5) The positions of the teaching principles and implementation measures in the general outline should be reversed. (6) The objectives of civic training are prescribed as follows: A. To cultivate children's noble character and good behavior; B. To cultivate children's ability to organize groups and the spirit of social service; C. To cultivate children's strong physique and happy emotions; D. To develop children's labor habits and interest in production. (7) The Civic Training Law: The group will formulate the main points of the civic training law and submit them to the standing committee for compilation.

(8) Detailed Items for Civic Training Operations: The standing committee will classify the existing materials and

create annual tables, send them to the committee members, set a deadline for reporting opinions, and then make a decision.

(II) Secondary School Group 115

Secondary School Group Decisions

(I) Total weekly self-study hours at school for each grade in junior high school: 13 hours for the first, second, third, and fifth semesters, and 14 hours for the fourth and sixth semesters. The following regulations are also stipulated: 1. Junior high school students' total daily class and self-study time is set at eight hours, calculated as 48 hours per week, excluding class time; the remaining time is for self-study at school. 2. Teachers must supervise and guide self-study time at school. 3. All students, whether boarding or day students, must participate in self-study at school. 4. Extracurricular sports and activities for students are not included in the self-study time at school. 5. The time for self-study at school and extracurricular sports activities may be slightly adjusted and flexibly arranged according to the season, day student/boarding student status, and other factors.

(II) Total weekly extracurricular activities and self-study hours for senior high school: 27 hours for the first, second, third, and fourth semesters, and 30 hours for the fifth and sixth semesters. The following regulations are also stipulated: 1. Senior high school students' total daily class, self-study, and extracurricular sports time is set at ten hours, calculated as 60 hours per week. 2. In addition to class time, one hour per day is designated for extracurricular sports, with the remaining time for self-study. 3. Teachers must supervise and guide both extracurricular sports and self-study time.

(III) Junior high school Chinese language will follow the original proposal, using both classical and vernacular Chinese.

(IV) For drawing, Xu Beihong advocated "teaching to the best of one's ability." As a result, "teaching to the best of one's ability" was implemented before teaching geometry in junior high school, and only pattern design and instrument use were taught in senior high school. (V) Except for courses such as Civics, Mineralogy, Agriculture, and Home Economics, which require separate drafting, all other course curricula have been revised and approved.

(VI) A member proposed during the meeting that since teachers are responsible for guiding self-study, self-study time should be compensated at the same rate as class time. As a result, the Ministry of Education stated that hourly pay in secondary schools could easily lead to abuse. The Ministry of Education is currently drafting salary guidelines for secondary school teachers.

▲ Experts Express Opinions on Secondary School Curriculum

Education experts from both primary and secondary school groups stated that the members of the secondary school group were able to uphold their positions, striving for the number of hours allocated to each subject and advocating for specialization in senior high school, which is commendable. However, curriculum development is a specialized field. It is best for experts from research departments to draft the curriculum, then gather opinions from experts in each subject before finalizing it, which would be more rational and avoid conflicts over each subject "sweeping snow from its own doorstep." Now that senior high school is divided into general, vocational, and teacher training tracks, the question arises whether the junior high school curriculum and hours decided upon this time have the function of exploring students' interests in employment, or are they only considering general track students who will continue their education? This is a question worthy of further study. Furthermore, the style of the secondary school curriculum standards generally uses classical Chinese, while textbooks for each subject, except for Chinese language, generally use vernacular Chinese, creating inconsistency.

It is indeed necessary to further discuss this matter, it is said.

▲ Teaching Hour Table for Each Semester of Junior and Senior High School

The Secondary School Group of the Primary and Secondary School Curriculum Standards Revision Conference, after three days of intense discussion, revised and approved one teaching hour table for each semester of junior and senior high school, and one elective course classification table for the three years of senior high school. These three tables are of great importance to the overall curriculum planning of secondary schools. They are reproduced below:

Students who select subjects from the first category cannot select subjects from the second category, and vice versa.

Shen Silian Reports on His Trip 116

▲ Rumors of Manchukuo's Participation in the World Games Are Completely False

▲ The Organizing Committee Has Earnestly Assured Consul General Huang

▲ The Dispatch of Our Country's Athletes Has Attracted Great Attention from Americans

Mr. Shen Silian, the representative of the International Olympic Committee member Wang Rutang and Fu Shizhi, wrote from Berkeley, California, on July 14th: Every time the ship I was on arrived at a port, news reporters often prepared small boats to greet us, especially in Japan and San Francisco, indicating that China's first participation in the World Games this time has attracted great attention. I heard many things about our country sending two athletes. Japanese newspapers were quite concerned about this, but their comments were mostly negative. In San Francisco, I met American and Chinese news reporters. When the ship arrived or the next day, newspapers published news about China's participation in this World Games. The overseas Chinese were particularly concerned about various news and Liu Changchun's actual participation. Liu's attendance will bring praise and respect from many people in China. I dare to say that.

After arriving here, I immediately visited Dr. Huang Yunsu, the Consul General of China. In his office, I saw the letters he exchanged with the organizing committee regarding the rumor that the organizing committee had recognized Manchukuo's participation in the Games. Based on the correspondence, the committee did not do this and never officially allowed them to participate in the Summer Olympics Committee. The committee assured Consul General Huang that all rumors were groundless. Although Shanghai's Western newspapers reported that the Chinese government had ordered Consul General Huang to represent China at the official opening ceremony of the Games, Dr. Huang Zhisu told me today that he had not received such an appointment. I hope he will eventually receive instructions from the central government, as I very much hope he can accompany me to Los Angeles.

The grand ceremony at the end of the month has been prepared. President Hoover will officiate the official opening ceremony. Governor Roosevelt of New York is also expected to attend. Hundreds of foreign athletes have already arrived in Los Angeles for their final training. Newspapers everywhere have special reports on the Summer Olympics. Tickets for various events can be purchased in various cities in the United States. Signs selling tickets are everywhere. The whole country knows about this grand event.

The United States is confident in track and field. This Saturday and Sunday, American athletes will hold national trials in California. Many world records have been eclipsed. There are many talented American runners.

The United States also hopes to win in swimming, but Japan is competing fiercely and may take second place. Japan's swimming team has great hope and believes they can secure the swimming title. It is too early to predict other sports. The registration deadline for all events is July 16. On the 12th, I registered Liu Changchun for the 100-meter, 200-meter, and 400-meter races. Although we don't have high hopes, this is a start, and hopefully a good one.

Sixth Day of the 10th World Games 117

New World Records Abound

▲ Javelin, Triple Jump, Women's 80-Meter Hurdles All Set World Records

The appearance of new world records is commonplace, as reporters have repeatedly stated. On the sixth day of the Games (i.e., the fifth day of track and field competitions), three more world records were set: (1) Finnish athlete Järvinen's javelin throw of 72.74 meters; (2) Japan's Nan's triple jump of 15.72 meters; (3) After American Didrikson set a world record of 143 feet 4 inches (43.688 meters) in the women's javelin throw, she set a new world record of 11.7 seconds in the women's 80-meter hurdles, shortening her previous time of 11.8 seconds in the preliminary round by another second. Setting world records is as easy as turning one's hand! The new records of the Olympic Games will be regarded as worthless, without any value. Reporters can only be speechless about this.

Los Angeles, April 4th (Telecommunications): The results of today's javelin final are as follows: First: Järvinen (Finland) 72.74 meters (New Olympic Record), Second: Sippala (Finland), Third: Penttilä (Finland), Fourth: Waumann (Germany), Fifth: Bradley (USA), Sixth: Chatzir (USA). Women's 80-Meter Hurdles Sets Another World Record 120

▲ Time of Only 11.7 Seconds

▲ Another Masterpiece by an American Woman

Los Angeles, April 4th (Telecommunications): In today's 80-meter women's hurdles final, Miss Didrikson of the United States finished first with a time of 11.7 seconds, setting a new world record. The previous world record was 12.2 seconds, held by Miss Cikloba of Czechoslovakia.

Los Angeles, April 4th (Telecommunications): The women's 80-meter hurdles final was held at 4:30 PM today. The results are as follows: First: Didrikson (USA) 11.7 seconds (New World Record), Second: Hoolu (USA), Third: Gulack (USA), Fourth: Siahla (USA), Fifth: Weaip (UK), Sixth: Wilson (Canada). Los Angeles, April 4th (Reuters): Miss Didrikson of the United States, who recently set a world record in the women's javelin throw, today set a new world record in the women's 80-meter hurdles with a time of only 11.7 seconds, surpassing her own world record of 11.8 seconds set in the preliminary round.

Miss Didrikson of Texas, USA, has set two new world records in women's track and field at this Games: (1) 80-meter hurdles in 11.7 seconds; (2) women's javelin throw of 143 feet 4 inches. She can be called the model of world female athletes, and the most honored athlete of this Games.

Nan Wins Triple Jump 121

▲ Achieves 15.72 Meters

A New World Record

▲ Oda Cries Due to Elimination

Los Angeles, April 4th (Reuters): Japan today won its first track and field event. After winning the triple jump, Chūhei Nanbu won the triple jump championship, breaking the record of 49 feet 10 and 13/16 inches set by Mikio Oda at the 9th Games in 1928, with a record of 51 feet 6 and 3/4 inches, setting a new world record. Los Angeles, April 4th (Telecommunications): The results of today's triple jump final are as follows: First: Chūhei Nanbu (Japan) 15.72 meters, Second: Svensson (Sweden) 15.32 meters, Third: Kenkichi Oshima (Japan) 15.12 meters, Fourth: FitzClarence (Ireland), Fifth: Badhas (Netherlands), Sixth: Solvas (USA). Nanbu's record of 15.72 meters is a new world record, not only breaking the Olympic record of 15.525 meters held by Viarda, but also breaking Oda's world record of 15.58 meters.

▲Oda Cries Due to Elimination. International hurdles star Mikio Oda, although competing despite illness, only jumped 14 and a half meters on his first and second attempts. Although he jumped on the third attempt, the pain was too great, and he could not jump again, leading to his elimination. At that time, tears of sadness welled up in his cheeks. When he saw Nanbu win first place, he rushed to Nanbu to express his deep gratitude and embraced each other to show their closeness. At this time, the Japanese flag was hoisted on the central flagpole, the national anthem was played, and the Japanese expatriates cheered and applauded non-stop. Then Oda and Nanbu, amidst great cheers, went hand in hand to the athletes' changing room.

▲The Finals: Los Angeles, April 4th (Telecommunications): At the beginning of the triple jump, Wass (USA) jumped 14.852 meters on his first attempt, Romero (USA) jumped 14.820 meters, and Ohman (USA) jumped 14.744 meters. At that time, Nanbu (Japan) had already jumped 15.074 meters, taking the lead. Oda jumped 14 and a half meters, and Oshima fouled. On the second attempt, Oda's leg pain flared up again, and he stopped at 14 and a half meters. Although Oshima jumped over 15 meters, he also fouled. Nanbu jumped 15.220 meters, and Svensson (Sweden) jumped 15.32 meters. On the third attempt, Oda made a final effort, with a tragic expression, after taking a deep breath, he only hobbled to the boundary line, unable to jump again due to the unbearable pain in his foot. The third attempt was then terminated. Fortunately, Nanbu and Oshima won first and third place respectively, comforting Nanbu's heart.

Chūhei Nanbu (Japan), who set a new world record in the triple jump, with a score of 15.72 meters.

▲ Finnish Athletes Will Maintain Their Championship

Los Angeles, April 4th (Telecommunications): The 5th is the seventh day of the Olympic Games. Victory in the decathlon has always been regarded as one of the highest honors in the Olympic Games. Since ancient times, champions in the decathlon have been said to have a sound physique to achieve victory. In the previous Games, first place went to Yrjö Mäkilä of Finland, second place went to A. J. Järvinen of Finland, and third place went to J. Doherty of the United States. In this Games, the Finnish army still has hopes of winning the championship. More than ten people have already registered, for events, including 100 meters, long jump, shot put, high jump, and 400 meters. The remaining five events will be held later (i.e., on the 6th and 7th). The rowing competition, which will begin at the Los Angeles wharf, is also a new competition. At the 9th Amsterdam Games, Norway was first, Sweden second, Denmark third, the Netherlands fourth, Czechoslovakia fifth, and Finland sixth. All Nordic countries have been selected for this Games. It is feared that the United Kingdom and the United States have no hope of winning the championship, and it will still belong to one of the Nordic countries.

In the modern pentathlon, the 5th will be for swimming. The athletes who participated in the equestrian and shooting events will now be in the water.

Minor Twist in the Davis Cup Finals This Year 126

▲ A Scene from Balotera vs. Allison

▲ Alleged Referee Error, but Still Proven Fair

In this year's Davis Cup tennis tournament, France and the United States competed in Paris. The focus of the outcome between the two countries was really Balotera's victory over Allison. When the two men were playing, some people thought that the service line judge mistakenly called Balotera's second serve a good ball, which prevented Allison from completing the last point of his winning set. The Davis Cup championship also shifted because of this. Although Mr. Giro, President of the French Tennis Association, understood that the umpire on the court had irrefutable power, he still announced the letters from the service line judge and the linesman to show impartiality. In the judge's letter, he said that Mr. Ba's second serve was right on the line and was considered valid. There were many difficult problems on the court, but this one was the easiest to solve. He had served as a Davis Cup referee for five years and had never made any mistakes. In the linesman's letter, he said that in his personal opinion, Mr. Ba's serve landed right on the line, without any objection, so he considered the judge's decision to be completely correct.

Page 11

Free Talk

Sayings of Uncle Ma, a 93-Year-Old Man

China's First Map 130

— Han Ji

When Haishenwai [Vladivostok] was taken by the Russians, no one knew where Haishenwai was, and even maps were hard to find. Speaking of maps, one must recall the historical records of the mapmaking during the reign of Emperor Kangxi of the Qing Dynasty, which is also found in the study of the spread of Catholicism in China. (In the 47th year of Kangxi's reign, priests were ordered to go to various parts of Mongolia and provinces of China to survey mountains, rivers, cities, and walls, and to draw maps using Western triangulation methods. Officials were also selected and dispatched to assist, and orders were sent to governors-general and governors to instruct local officials under their jurisdiction to provide all necessary supplies.) ········

[From the 47th year of Kangxi, more than ten priests, including Bai Jin [Joachim Bouvet], Lei Xiaosi [Jean-Baptiste Régis], Du Demei [Pierre Jartoux], Pan Ru [Matteo Ripa], and Demano [Xavier Ehrenbert Fridelli], went to various provinces to draw maps. They started from outside the passes, then extended to the interior provinces, and it took nine years for the map to be completed. It was named "Complete Map of the Imperial Territory." In addition to the general map, there were also provincial maps. Bai Jin and others presented them to the Emperor for review, and they were greatly praised by the Emperor.] ········ [In the 58th year of Kangxi, the Emperor held the map and said to the Grand Secretary of the Inner Cabinet, Jiang Tingxi:] ·· [This map took me more than thirty years of effort to complete. The mountains and rivers are all consistent with the Yu Gong [Tribute of Yu]. You can show this map to the Nine Ministers for their examination.]

The Nine Ministers requested to be granted a copy, and the Emperor approved. Thus, the map drawn by the priests was widely circulated, covering the entire country. This was truly the beginning of maps in China. The maps drawn by Matteo Ricci in the past had many omissions, and the maps drawn by the Chinese were disorganized and full of errors, not worth a scholar's laugh. To this day, Chinese and foreign people who draw maps of China generally use the Kangxi map as a blueprint.]

Emperor Kangxi took this first map of China very seriously, just as Napoleon viewed the Civil Code. Originally, Napoleon, in exile on Saint Helena, on the eve of his death, said to his loyal general Montholon ·· [In my life, I have won hundreds of battles, but the Battle of Waterloo completely ruined my achievements, reducing them to nothing. Only this Civil Code is my sole success.]

Emperor Kangxi loved that map so much that he specially ordered someone to make a white jade eight-immortal table. On the surface of the white jade table, a map inlaid with gold was carved with extremely fine craftsmanship. This is a story not recorded in historical records. During the Anglo-French Allied Forces invasion, the British transported this white jade eight-immortal table to Shanghai. I personally saw this map inlaid with gold and white jade. Later, I heard that the white jade eight-immortal table somehow sank into the Mediterranean Sea and never made it to England.

This is a last resort. Please forgive our readers who love it.

Records of What I Saw and Heard in Nanyang [Southeast Asia] 131

— Mian Han

The Snake Temple on Penang Island Penang Island, also known as Pinang, is one of the three states of the British Straits Settlements. It is the garden of the Nanyang Islands. On the island, there is an area called "Shen Qi Ke Long" [Sungai Keluang]. The famous Snake Temple is located there. In the temple, snakes gather in groups of three or five, coiling around shrubs or winding on stone steps. They do not bite or run away when they see people. They raise their heads and stick out their tongues, appearing content and at ease. The snakes are mostly yellow, and there are approximately several hundred of them. No one knows the exact number. The snakes are extremely tame and never harm people. Even if someone touches or strokes them, they do not react in any way. The snakes have a habit of eating chicken eggs. If a guest buys eggs to eat, they nod their heads to express their gratitude to the guest. The snakes use their sharp teeth to break a hole in the end of the egg and suck out all the yolk and white. They eat quickly without breaking the egg. The locals believe that the temple has many snakes that are harmless to people because it is blessed by a deity. Therefore, the incense in this temple is very prosperous. Every year, the sixth day of the first lunar month is a major day for the local people to worship at the temple (meaning it is a festival). Worshippers enter and exit the Snake Temple in an endless stream, expressing their superstition to the fullest. New visitors to Nanyang, hearing that the snakes in the temple, although venomous, are not poisonous, often go to the temple to pay their respects. Therefore, the person guarding the temple takes the opportunity to sell incense, candles, paper ingots, and chicken eggs, and their income is said to be quite good.

▲ The Singapore Botanic Gardens The Singapore Botanic Gardens is located on Holland Road in the Bukit Timah district. It covers an area of approximately 350 acres. The garden is densely covered with trees and grass, and there are ponds, offices, libraries, and experiment rooms. The buildings are exquisitely built and fully equipped. The garden was founded in 1874. The rubber trees of Nanyang are the result of experiments in the aforementioned experiment rooms. The garden is also famous for this. After entering the garden gate, proceed along the asphalt road. On the left, you can see tropical plants such as the sago palm and the coconut palm. On the right, the terrain is undulating, and the green lawn fills the eyes. The high ground of the hill is like a platform. High trees that reach the sky are planted all around. Walking here on a moonlit night is like being in another world, no longer in the human realm. Turning from the foot of the hill, you will encounter a pond. In the pond, there is a patch of grass more than ten feet square, on which mango trees are planted. Legend has it that the Tang Dynasty monk Xuanzang was the first to introduce mangoes to China. Whether he brought them back to China from here is unknown. On the shore of the pond, there is a durian tree, which is very strange in appearance. Proceeding from the pond, there is a slope. On the side of the road, there is a bodhi tree with leaves shaped like purses, as well as betel nut trees and sorrowless trees. In Sanskrit, the sorrowless tree is called Ashoka, and Indians revere it like a god. Going further to the right, you can enter the office. Turning left will return you to the asphalt road. Proceeding to the right of the crossroads, there is a shade house. Going west from here, you can reach Coconut Valley. There are many varieties of coconuts here, dazzling the eyes. There are so-called ivory coconuts, sugar coconuts, big-leaf coconuts, wax-flying coconuts, fan-leaf coconuts, king coconuts, and shell-leaf coconuts, etc. Passing Coconut Valley, you can exit the garden. This garden is rich in tropical plants. Anyone who studies plants will be delighted to see it. Behind the garden gate, in the woods, there are many monkeys crouching on the road, not afraid of people. They even kowtow to beg for things. If you try to catch them, they will run away. They move as fast as lightning and disappear in an instant.

The Riddle of Hollywood 132

— Lao Ren

Who knows, Locke is the comedian of Hollywood. Every movie fan has in their minds all sorts of humorous actions of this gentleman. Recently, a lawsuit between a real and fake Locke suddenly occurred in Los Angeles. What exactly is the truth in the gourd? This riddle has yet to be broken. As for Huang Amei, I'm afraid more people know her, because she is China's only star overseas. Last month, she was entangled by a strange old lady who insisted on being her mother. It's really funny.

▲ Lawsuit between real and fake Lockes The lawsuit between the real and fake Lockes has been going on for several years. The New York court has been trying this case for a long time but has not been able to resolve it. Both sides insist on their own versions of events, and the argument is getting fiercer. The plaintiff insists that the Locke who is currently making movies is fake and should be charged with impersonation. He petitioned the authorities, saying, "I, Burchard, was born in Nebraska as Harold Lloyd. The imposter movie star must be prohibited from using the name Harold Lloyd." At the time, the authorities ruled in favor of the defendant because the plaintiff did not have sufficient evidence. Unexpectedly, last month, the plaintiff's case was revived and he filed a second lawsuit with the court. Locke has already spent thousands of dollars dealing with him. There are currently no results. However, the Locke production company is extremely busy answering letters from all over the world asking about the lawsuit every day. The strangest thing is that Locke received a forged letter saying, "Your feet are worth twelve million dollars. Please send down some." From this, we can infer the key to this impersonation lawsuit.

▲ Huang Amei's Mother The Chinese female star Huang Amei has had a considerable history in Hollywood. She lives on Figueroa Street. In addition to her parents, there is also a younger sister named Mary in the family. One day, Amei received a letter with the following content: "Amei, please come to 908 North Country Street. Mother." Amei was extremely surprised. She immediately consulted with her lawyer. To avoid the danger of kidnapping, she reported it to the police, who sent three detectives to accompany her. When they arrived at the location specified in the letter, they saw an elderly woman who grasped Amei's hand and said incessantly, "Ten years ago, I had a beloved daughter who suddenly disappeared from China. I searched for her without success. By chance, I saw your beautiful face on the screen, and it resembled my beloved daughter. That's why I came from thousands of miles away to meet you." Although Amei listened to her words, comforted her, and left. On the third day, the beautiful tale of the Chinese old woman searching for her daughter thousands of miles away was spread throughout Hollywood.

— Hu

Mr. Wu Zhong, a native of Suzhou, has been engaged in the writing profession for many years. He has connections with people in the literary and art circles in Shanghai. Recently, he has collaborated with the martial arts star Zheng Chaofan to create a literary and art tri-weekly publication called "Ji Bao." The selection of articles is strict, and the materials are new and unique. It will create a new style in small newspapers. It is said that it will be published soon.

Worth Introducing Domestic Goods Factories (18) 134

— He, Gong, Xing

(29) Glassware Factory

There are more than a dozen manufacturers of glassware in Shanghai. The larger ones include Zhonghua Fengji, Pudong No. 1 Factory, Gongyi Renhe, Qianyi Bingtai, Shanghai Xiechang, Sanyi, and Jiangji. The Xin'ya Chemical Pharmaceutical Factory also produces glass bottles and watch glasses. These types of bottles for holding liquid medicines must be made of hard glass, otherwise the medicine will undergo a chemical reaction and the bottle will break. In our country, only Xin'ya produces hard glass bottles and watch glasses. The rest mainly produce lampshades.

The raw material for making lampshades is glass sand, which is produced in Suqian, Jiangsu, and Lufeng, Guangdong. Analyzing it, its components are approximately manganese feldspar, stone powder, sulfurized charcoal, sodium sulfate, sand, potassium carbonate, calcium carbonate, lead carbonate, alkali, etc. However, manufacturers in Shanghai mostly buy broken glass pieces and remelt them to make lampshades, taking advantage of the convenience and low price. However, if you want to make hard glass, you must add raw materials.

A furnace is required to melt the materials. The furnace is made of pot ash and wood. The fuel is charcoal or bituminous coal. After four or five hours of burning, the material in the pot melts into a liquid. Workers gather around the furnace and dip the end of a glass tube into the pot. After a little liquid adheres, they take it out. Seeing the liquid forming a ball at the end of the tube, they blow it into a bubble shape and then put it into a mold. They blow it again, and the lampshade is formed. The molds are all made of iron. One mold forms two or three lampshades. After pouring them out, they are opened with a lathe and polished with a grinding wheel. Then they are placed in a baking oven for another baking. Then this shade is durable and can be sold. Prices vary widely, and sales are better in the interior. However, when manufacturing lampshades, although there are molds, the technique of mouth-blowing and hand-turning must be skillful. It is impossible without highly skilled workers. The wages are about 50 or 60 yuan per person per month.

The Japanese have established Bao Cheng in Shanghai, in Gujiawan, and San Gong, on Wuzhou Road. The Baoshan Glass Factory on Yokohama Road is a Sino-Japanese joint venture with a capital of 300,000 to 500,000 yuan. It is the largest glass factory in Shanghai.

Recording the Sound of Clock Strikes at Ancient Temples (66) 135

— Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhai Tian

63

I said: "Changes in individual attitudes are certainly possible, but relying solely on individual efforts to promote the work-study corps is unreliable and slow. China has now reached a critical juncture of life and death. The times will not allow us to leisurely shed this traditional snake skin. I am impatient to wait for the natural spread of this work-study corps. I am eager to hear you talk about that compulsory dissemination."

Mr. Zhu said: "Compulsory dissemination is inevitable dissemination. The inevitable dissemination of the work-study corps comes from two paths. (1) The general phenomenon in the country now is that the number of school-age children who want to enter elementary school but cannot exceeds the capacity of new elementary schools by several times; the number of elementary school graduates who want to enter middle school but cannot exceeds the capacity of new middle schools by several times; the number of middle school graduates who want to enter university but cannot exceeds the capacity of new universities by several times. New universities, new middle schools, and new elementary schools are unable to add more places, so where do the majority of students who cannot pass the entrance exams to universities, middle schools, and elementary schools go? Their thirst for knowledge has been awakened, and the facts will not allow them to enter purely academic schools. This work-study corps is just right for their needs. (2) Traditional universities, elementary schools, and middle schools only consume and do not produce. The people they cultivate are also naturally those who can only consume and cannot produce. No one wants people who can only consume and cannot produce. Nankai University once had a discussion about 'rotating education.' The so-called 'rotating education' meant that teachers taught students, and students became teachers in rotation, all circling within the walls of the school. Now, even this rotating circle is unreliable. It is already difficult for university graduates to become elementary school teachers, and middle school graduates are even less likely to do so. When there is a vacancy for an elementary school teacher, there are sometimes dozens of candidates. This clearly shows us that traditional schools have reached the end of their rope. If useful things are overproduced, they still cannot be sold, let alone waste! Traditional schools originally produced useless people, which were difficult to sell. Fortunately, there were positions for teachers in lower-level schools, allowing them to dump their products. Now that even this dumping route has been blocked, can we still produce useless people? These facts are bound to come, inevitably forcing the entire nation to awaken, and inevitably forcing the entire nation to find another way of life and not allowing them to hesitate for even a moment at this crossroads. At this critical juncture of life and death, the entire nation may issue a general mobilization order, requiring everyone to live a work-study corps life together, in which case turning danger into safety will be as easy as turning one's hand."

Anecdotes from the Examination Hall 136

— Yang Yu Sheng

There were two pedantic brothers in the county. The elder brother lived in the south of the city, and the younger brother lived in the north of the county. They were both old scholars from elementary schools. Last autumn, they went to Nanjing together to take the examination for certification. The first exam was arithmetic. The examiner ordered them to answer the question: "Today there are 112 taels of meat. How many catties [jin] is that?" The brothers, who were sitting next to each other, could not decide on the answer and began to argue. Soon the argument became more intense. They even forgot themselves, and the noise startled everyone. They almost started a fistfight. The examiner was angry and stopped them. He asked them what the matter was. The elder brother stepped forward and said, "The city scale is slightly less than 15 taels per catty, and the county scale is slightly more than 16 taels per catty. I don't know if this 112 taels of meat should be measured with the city scale or the county scale. It's a matter of 'a few taels of meat,' [which] 'must not be brushed aside.' That's why we argued." The examiner fell over laughing and ordered them to leave and dismissed them.

The decline of national studies has reached its extreme today. When a certain university in Beiping came to Shanghai to recruit students this time, in order to promote national studies, all applicants to the Faculty of Arts, in addition to the particularly obscure classical Chinese exam questions, were asked to answer a name for "Sun Wukong." [The Monkey King] Applicants were caught off guard and were all forced to put down their pens and politely decline. An older student heard this and said, "What's so difficult about that? 'Hu Shi' is an acceptable answer." As the saying goes, "Those who can do it find it easy, those who cannot do it find it difficult." That's what it means.

Financial Bullion Experiences Sharp Drop 137

▲ Down by Seven Taels Yesterday, there was a sudden slump in the bullion market, with dealers showing signs of weakening and prices fluctuating. Overall, there was a difference of more than eight taels throughout the day, followed by a sharp drop of seven taels, a dramatic change unseen for many days. Supply exceeded demand from all sides, and initially the market was relatively stable, with no movement in the silver market, but the exchange rate suddenly plummeted. As a result, both official and unofficial foreign exchange rates loosened, causing this sudden change in the market. There were occasional fluctuations of two taels, but the 740 tael mark was eventually broken. The market became increasingly sluggish, with both the British and American exchange rates becoming unusually loose, and the market almost collapsed. Prices continued to fall by four to five taels, and finally ended at around thirty-six taels. Rumor has it that a certain bank purchased more than 300 bars of spot bullion at a price of around 742 taels. The daily situation is recorded below:

▲ Opening Price Increased by Three Cents The market opened relatively flat in the early morning, up slightly by three cents, at 743 taels and 8 cents. Although the silver price and other factors did not show any gains or losses, the sudden drop in the exchange rate by 2.375 points allowed the gold price to be maintained. The next price was 44 taels, with Yifeng Yongwu and others buying in. Subsequently, Hengxing, Yuanyuanmao, Yongzhi, Fengyong, and others came to sell, and the exchange rate was initially flat, with British gold at half a penny for August settlement and Shanghai for October at 6.6875. The US dollar was selling at 30 yuan for the near term, and the gold price retreated by more than one tael. At 9:30, it was 42.5 taels. The internal plate for the US dollar in September was 30 yuan and 6.25 cents for both purchases and sales. Before long, Wu Pin, Setou [a type of trading], and Hengxing, Yuanchong, Kangyong, Yuanyuan, Dayong, and others dumped their holdings, and the price dropped by more than two taels. At nearly 10 o'clock, it was 40 taels and 9 cents. Yu Hongjun's Reply to the Joint Committee 162

▲ Clarifying Okazaki's Original Letter

Recently, Okazaki, the representative of the Japanese Joint Committee, sent a letter to Keeningham, the chairman of the Joint Committee, stating that the Chinese government had suddenly reorganized troops into police in Zhabei and other places, and had also equipped them with field artillery. He requested that the Joint Committee pay close attention to this matter. At that time, Keeningham immediately sent a copy of Okazaki's original letter to Yu Hongjun, the Chinese representative. Mr. Yu immediately sent a reasoned reply to the Joint Committee, stating: "I received your letter, which included a letter from Mr. Okazaki, the Japanese representative, to your chairman. After reading it, I am extremely surprised. I do not understand why the Japanese representative finds it necessary to interfere with the Chinese government's measures to maintain local public security. The Chinese government has consistently treated friendly nations with sincerity and openness, which is evident to both the Japanese government and people. However, the Japanese representative still makes reckless speculations, which is deeply regrettable. The Chinese government has the right to adopt any of the best measures to maintain local order and tranquility, which I must repeatedly declare. However, the Chinese government, in exercising its inherent sovereignty, has no need to disguise troops as police."

A Large Number of Japanese Warships Arrive in Shanghai 163

▲ Shanghai Has as Many as Fifteen Japanese Warships

The Japanese Navy Fleet of the Yangtze River has recently been ordered by Sakonji, the commander of the Third Fleet, to redeploy its forces, concentrating a portion of the departing warships in Shanghai. At the same time, it has also ordered warships stationed upstream of the Yangtze River to protect Japanese vessels and safeguard the promotion of Japanese goods. The details are as follows:

▲ Japanese Warships of the Yangtze River Redeployed to Shanghai The destroyers "Yanagi," "Momo," "Kashi," and "Hinoki" of the 24th Squadron of the Japanese Navy were redeployed to Shanghai during the January 28th Incident. After the ceasefire, they joined the First Overseas Dispatch Squadron and were stationed in Nanjing, Daye, and other places. Since the "Blood Soul Corps" incident in Shanghai, the Japanese Naval Ministry had already sent all four warships of the 15th Squadron to Shanghai. Now, it has telegraphed the light cruiser "Tenryu," stationed in Nanjing, and the four destroyers of the 24th Squadron to Shanghai. At 10:10 AM yesterday, the "Tenryu" entered the port. At 12:35 PM, the four destroyers arrived at Wusong. In the afternoon, they sailed into the Huangpu River and anchored in the Yangshupu area.

▲ A Significant Increase in Japanese Warships in the Huangpu River After the withdrawal of Japanese troops after the war, only three Japanese warships remained in Shanghai. Since the arrival of the four warships of the 15th Squadron, as of yesterday, there are a total of fifteen Japanese warships in the Huangpu River, including "Tsushima," "Hozu," "Izumo," "Ataka," "Hira," "Seta," and the destroyers "Yanagi," "Momo," "Kashi," "Hinoki," "Usu," "Kuzu," "Fuji," and "Ogi." Their berthing locations stretch from the Huangpu River to the Zhabei River mouth. The "Urakaze," on the other hand, has been redeployed to Nanjing. The Japanese naval presence in Shanghai has once again greatly increased.

▲ The Situation of Japanese Goods Being Transported to Hankou After the resumption of loading on the 26th of last month, a large quantity of Japanese goods was exported on the Yangtze River. Recently, after the warning from the "Blood Soul Corps," most unscrupulous merchants dare not openly transport them. The route for Japanese goods on the Yangtze River has once again been halted. However, inferior Japanese goods are still being shipped to the Yangtze River in a continuous stream. A large quantity is stored at the postal pier. On the 4th of this month, the Japanese vessel "Xiangyang Maru" resumed normal loading and transport. It is said that Japanese merchants have consulted with the Shanghai-based navy and are still following the navy's method of controlling Japanese vessels on the Yangtze River from last month. For any Japanese goods loaded to Wuhu, Jiujiang, Hankou, Yichang, Changsha, and other ports, the First Overseas Dispatch Squadron headquarters will secretly telegraph the Japanese warships stationed at those ports. When the Japanese goods arrive at the docks for unloading, the navy will use its strength to assist in unloading and bringing them ashore. Therefore, inferior goods can once again be transported as usual.

The "Blood Soul Corps" Again Uses Bombs to Warn Two Businesses 164

▲ Jiu Shen and Yong Yu Each Receive a Bomb

The Shanghai "Blood Soul Corps" has discovered that Jiu Shen Yarn Shop in Dongde Lane, North Suzhou Road, and Yong Yu Cotton Shop in Tongfang Lane, Shilu, are still secretly selling Japanese goods. Therefore, yesterday (the 5th), they sent a bomb to each of the stores and left a warning note, roughly stating: "If you continue to sell Japanese goods, our final bullets will be merciless." The original notes are recorded below: (1) Note to Yong Yu Cotton Shop: "Yong Yu store owner, be warned. You still do not know how to repent and dare to sell enemy goods. We have left a bomb. ▲ To Warn Against Selling Japanese Goods

The Maochang Foreign Goods Store, located at 347 Minguo Road in the French Concession, continues to sell Japanese goods. At 9:05 PM last night, someone suddenly threw a bomb into the store. The company should be informed to issue a statement on the front page of the Shen Bao and Xin Wen newspapers for three days, stating that they will never again sell inferior sugar. If they do not accept the proposal, they will be expelled. (2) Handling the case of the sealed up Japanese refined sugar, as instructed by the general meeting. (5) Committee member Yang reported that smuggled sugar from Liuhe and Zhaopu was being sold in the interior. It was decided to petition the Customs Administration to investigate and ban it. (6) The chairman proposed that it has been heard that sugar substitutes sold on the market contain toxic substances. It was proposed to purchase a sample and send it to the Social Affairs Bureau for testing. It was decided to purchase a bottle and send it to the Health Bureau for testing. If it contains toxic substances, the public should be warned not to purchase it in the newspapers to emphasize health. (7) Reorganizing regulations. It was decided that the payment period for sugar purchased by various merchant groups should follow industry regulations and should not be delayed. The silver discount should be 5 qian per 1,000 taels and should not be deducted more. All samples stored should be cancelled and no more silver should be deducted. All members should be notified to comply.

▲ Miscellaneous Grains and Oil Cakes Association The Shanghai Miscellaneous Grains and Oil Cakes Association held a meeting of members yesterday afternoon at 4 PM to thoroughly investigate whether members were purchasing Japanese rice. Cai Yukun chaired the meeting, reported on the proceedings, and read aloud the letters received from members reporting their rice stocks, then handed them over for discussion. (1) Regarding the case of the foreign rice stored in various warehouses by Tongxingtai, which has already been sampled by the association and should be publicly inspected, it was decided that the registration book of Tongxingtai was checked against the dates and quantities of the foreign rice that arrived at various warehouses. It was found that, except for three receipts where the dates of loading and arrival did not match, the rest were consistent. Now, the rice samples collected by the association have been publicly inspected and confirmed to be old rice. This is confirmed by the company's previous letter, which stated that this foreign rice was ordered before the September 18th Incident last year. This cannot be said to be untrue. Regarding the three receipts where the dates of loading and arrival did not match, it is considered suspicious and should be banned. The receipts that match the association's registration shall be allowed to be bought and sold. However, the warehouse receipts must be sent to the association for verification and stamping before being announced to the market to show seriousness. Regarding the rice transported from Hong Kong, the company should also send the bill of lading to the association for verification and stamping. If it is indeed loaded by Tongxingtai, it may be allowed to be bought and sold according to the previous method. (2) Regarding the letter from the North Office of the Bean and Rice Industry, which stated that Shu Zhanyuan, the manager of Rentai Trading Co. in Zhabei, was falsely accused by a certain tabloid of transporting Japanese rice and should be thoroughly investigated, it was decided that the truth of the matter must be thoroughly investigated. Chairman Cai was invited to meet with Committee Member Jiang Hongbin of the Bean and Rice Industry Association and the responsible personnel of the North Office at 10 AM on the 7th to thoroughly investigate the foreign rice stored by Rentai Trading Co. and report to the association for verification. (3) Regarding the letter from the Heji Rice Mill stating that it was reported that they had purchased Japanese rice and requesting a thorough investigation and correction, it was decided to reply to the mill that since they did not purchase it, they should send a letter to correct it themselves. The meeting adjourned after 6 PM.

The City Chamber of Commerce Establishes a Special Committee to Study the Abolition of the Tael and the Adoption of the Yuan 169

▲ Twelve Opinions Received from Various Industries

▲ Second Meeting Scheduled for the 10th of This Month

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, after its third Executive Committee meeting, decided to establish a special research committee on the issue of abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan. Zhu Wenqi, Fang Jiaobo, Ma Jiliang, Luo Qinghua, Lu Wenshao, Chen Zheqing, and Pei Yunqing were appointed as members of the committee. On one hand, opinions from various industries were collected as a basis for research. As of yesterday, a total of 12 opinions had been received from various industries. The research committee held its first committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 2 PM. Committee members Zhu Wenqi, Fang Jiaobo, Ma Jiliang, Luo Qinghua, and Lu Wenshao attended. Zhu Wenqi chaired the meeting. The secretariat first reported on the opinions received from various industries one by one. After detailed discussion by the committee members, it was decided that (1) the issue is of great importance. The association will first send the received opinions to the committee members for detailed consideration; (2) The association is collecting opinions from chambers of commerce across the country. They should be collected and submitted to the committee meeting for joint research next Monday; (3) The second committee meeting is scheduled for next Wednesday (the 10th).

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency interviewed Zhu Wenqi, the director of the research committee, yesterday, asking him to express his views on the abolition of the tael and the adoption of the yuan. According to him, from an objective standpoint and based on economic theory, he advocates that (1) the weight and fineness of the new silver coins should be based on the silver coins with the lowest silver fineness currently circulating on the market. The phenomenon of bad money driving out good money is theoretically and practically unavoidable. If bad money can circulate on the market, good silver coins will be melted down. Therefore, after the appearance of Yuan Shikai silver coins, Jiangnan silver coins decreased. After the appearance of Sun Yat-sen silver coins, Yuan Shikai silver coins gradually disappeared. Therefore, if the fineness of the new silver coins is higher than that of the bad coins circulating on the market, there will inevitably be the problem of manufacturing on one hand and melting down on the other hand. Conversely, if, as advocated by Dexi, all kinds of mixed silver coins are recalled after the implementation of the new currency, there will naturally be no problem; (2) How to regulate the conversion ratio between silver tael contracts and silver coins during the valid period? He advocates the following methods: (A) The government issues an order that, for example, if the tael is abolished on January 1, 1933, then all previous silver tael contracts will be converted at the market price on December 31, 1932; (B) The government orders that, for example, if the abolition of the tael is implemented on September 1 of next year, then silver tael contracts can still be converted at the market price during this one-year period. For long-term contracts, the two parties can negotiate a compromise price, or the local chamber of commerce can negotiate a compromise price and ask the government to approve it; (3) What methods should be adopted to make the general public understand and trust this change? He believes that the opinions of the money industry and Gerhard should be adopted, such as: (A) The issuance of banknotes should have at least 60% reserve cash and should not be offset by other items; (B) Public groups should conduct public inspections at any time; (C) Free transportation; (D) The Central Mint should be the only mint in China, and all other factories should be dismantled; (4) He believes that the cost of minting new silver coins should be borne by the people, as stipulated in the Three People's Principles. Germany, France, and Japan have all done this. If the government bears the cost, the people can melt the new coins at any time to replace silver. To illustrate, silver shops do not need to buy silver bars, which requires more procedures. They only need to melt silver coins for use, while the state must process and mint them at a great loss. The above are his personal opinions, which will be contributed to the research committee for reference.

Shanghai and England Can Communicate by Wireless Telephone 170

According to the Zi Lin Daily, on Wednesday evening, the Italian postal ship "Conte Rosso" invited many celebrities from Shanghai to a dinner to see the newly installed wireless telephone. The Italian Minister Count Ciano personally made a phone call to Rome, talking with his father, the Minister of Communications, for a while. He then switched to Bolzano, a town 1,000 miles from Rome, to talk with his mother and sister. Both were very clear. The wireless telephone machine was produced by the Marconi Company and is the same as the ones installed on the English liner "Queen" and the "White Plains", both of which are very beautiful. At that time, the terrestrial line was borrowed from Rome to London. However, because there was no prior consultation, the London operator initially refused to transfer the call. When Count Ciano informed his father of this situation, a reply was received within a few minutes. The Italian Ministry of Communications had contacted the London Postal Authority, and the British Postal Authority had obtained permission from the British Foreign Office to open the telephone line between London and Rome for one hour, preparing to transfer the telephone calls from Shanghai. So, a re-test was performed last night (the 4th). A reporter from the London Times in Shanghai spoke to the London Post Office, asking them to transfer the call to the

Page 14

Times newspaper office. At that time, the reporter wanted to speak directly with the Times newspaper, but was restricted by government regulations and asked the post office staff to forward the message. In addition, the reporter also had a private telegram, which was also entrusted to the London Post Office staff for delivery.

Reuters, London, 5th: Last night, the Italian postal ship "Conte Rosso" in Shanghai spoke with the Minister of Communications in Rome via wireless telephone. Subsequently, a reporter from the London Times stationed in Shanghai spoke with London on the ship, which was very clear. However, the call was suddenly interrupted because the call between Shanghai and London had not been tested by the authorities. This morning, the Times published an editorial asking the public to pay attention to this matter, criticizing the post office for adhering to old rules and failing to cooperate with the Italian Minister of Communications in a spirit of enlightenment. The newspaper also advocated the rapid development of wireless telephone services between China and Britain, as this is extremely important for commerce.

City Chamber of Commerce Strives to Recover Pilotage Rights 171

▲ Vacancies for Pilots Should Be Filled by Chinese

▲ Chamber of Commerce Representatives Should Join the Committee

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Shipping Affairs Office, stating: Sirs, It is a common practice in various countries around the world to select their own nationals for the position of pilot. In the seventh year of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty, our country established general regulations for pilots at various seaports, allowing Chinese citizens and nationals of treaty countries who wished to become pilots to be employed equally. This open approach was unique to our country and not bound by treaties. Furthermore, the employment of foreign pilots at the mouth of the Yangtze River is not mentioned in the general regulations for pilots at various seaports, and has no legal basis. However, over time, foreign pilots have forgotten their place, gradually seeking to seize power and exclude Chinese from participating, reversing the roles of guest and host, causing resentment among Chinese. Since the tenth year of the Republic of China, there has been a movement to reclaim pilotage rights. Your office should be aware of these circumstances. According to the general regulations for pilots at various seaports, the pilot profession is under your office's jurisdiction, and as a Chinese government agency, you should strive to realize matters beneficial to the Chinese nation and people. We propose that your office instruct the foreign pilot association to: (1) Regardless of whether the association expands the number of pilots in the future or when vacancies arise, all replacements and trainees should be Chinese; (2) The association's previous promise to add five Chinese members should not be empty talk but should be realized promptly; (3) Since the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce already occupies a seat on the association's committee, our Chamber of Commerce should also be allowed to join a member to ensure fairness. We respectfully submit this letter, requesting your office to investigate and handle it accordingly. Addressed to the Jianghai Customs Shipping Affairs Office.

General Overview of Municipal Fiscal Revenue and Expenditure for the 20th Year 174

▲ Deficit of Over 1.1 Million Yuan

Yesterday, a reporter, seeking to inquire about the city's treasury revenue and expenditure, visited the responsible personnel of the Municipal Finance Bureau. They provided detailed information about the fiscal revenue and expenditure figures for the 20th year and the impact of the January 28th Incident, which is recorded below for the reference of those concerned about the city's finances. (1) The revenue for the 20th year was over 8.21 million yuan, an increase of over 1 million yuan compared to the 19th year, making it the highest revenue in the city's fiscal history. If not for the results of reorganizing old taxes throughout the year following the January 28th Incident, the total revenue could have reached 9 million yuan. (2) The expenditure for the 20th year was over 9.33 million yuan, exceeding the budget by over 1 million yuan, and an increase of over 1.7 million yuan compared to the 19th year. The excessive expenditure on temporary expenses (totaling over 2.5 million yuan), particularly the special expenses and rehabilitation costs after the Shanghai Incident, was the largest contributor. Compared to the 19th year, it was approximately 1 million yuan higher, and even exceeded the temporary budget for the 20th year by over 1.47 million yuan. This led to an extraordinary strain on the city's treasury. At the end of the year, the revenue and expenditure were balanced, resulting in a deficit of over 1.1 million yuan, which must be carried over to the next year for offset. The bureau has prepared a comparative table of revenue and expenditure calculations for the 20th and 19th years and submitted it to the mayor for review.

The United States can deeply observe China's progress. For example, in a large public gathering, one may feel that one is walking very slowly, but observers can see that one is progressing very quickly. I believe that China's current progress is the same as the United States' progress at that time. Therefore, the United States is eager to know how China is progressing. I have recently had several meetings with Chinese officials and feel that the Chinese authorities are paying great attention to this exposition and have very important proposals. I am also very willing to accept them sincerely."

Method for Generating Chinese Committee Members of the Land Committee 177

▲ Municipal Government Receives Reply from American Consul General Cunningham

▲ Immediately Forwarding Letter to the Ratepayers' Association for Review

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Land Committee, according to the resolution of the Western ratepayers' annual meeting on April 13th of this year, added two Chinese committee members. British Consul General Brenan and American Consul General Cunningham visited Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government two weeks ago to seek his opinion. Mayor Wu expressed not only his agreement but also his belief that it was necessary. Recently, American Consul General and Senior Consul Cunningham formally notified the Municipal Government in writing and regarding the method of producing members, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government sent a special letter to the Chinese ratepayers' association seeking their opinion. The original letter is recorded as follows: Sirs, Regarding the case of adding Chinese committee members to the Land Committee of the Public Concession, we have received a letter from the acting secretary of the Municipal Council stating that the Council has given the matter its attention. This matter has been forwarded. We have now received a letter from American Consul General and Senior Consul Cunningham stating that the Western ratepayers passed the following resolution at the annual meeting on April 13th of this year: This meeting considers the addition of two Chinese committee members to the Land Committee to be an appropriate move. Therefore, the Municipal Council is authorized and instructed to present everything to the relevant countries so that the Land Committee can add two Chinese committee members. The Shanghai Western Ratepayers' Association also stated that in addition to presenting the resolution to the relevant authorities, it hopes to protect the rights of Chinese ratepayers who are not owners. The rights of Chinese ratepayers are best protected by special regulations: (A) One of the two newly added Chinese committee members of the Land Committee must be appointed by the Chinese Ratepayers' Association. The appointee must not be an owner or a representative of an owner. The remainder are to be appointed by a meeting of Chinese owners. (B) In order to determine the qualifications of Chinese committee members of the Land Committee in accordance with the above principles, candidates for Chinese committee members must be selected after agreement between the Municipal Council and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, and between the Municipal Council and the Chinese Owners' Association.) Before the above resolutions and their attachments are implemented, Article 6(a) of the Yangjingbang Regulations must be amended. In accordance with Article 28 of the Yangjingbang Regulations, all construction and modification matters must be agreed upon by the consuls of the various countries and the Chinese local officials. Therefore, this Senior Consul requests that Your Excellency the Mayor consider the above proposals as soon as possible, and we hope that you will inform us of whether or not you agree. In accordance with the order to examine the case and notify the Ratepayers' Association, this letter is sent. We hope that your association will respond quickly to the letter's opinions and return them to the government for handling.

Dutch Merchants in Java Reject the Aiboer Electric Light Bulb 179

▲ Various Groups are Greatly Indignant

The Chinese Aiboer Electric Appliance Factory has been in operation for many years, specializing in the manufacture of electric light bulbs, electric fans, and motors. Its products are sold throughout the country and exported to various ports in Southeast Asia, such as Siam and Burma. Due to their low prices and excellent quality, they are very popular among the local people. In Java, Dutch East Indies, they are sold through the Chinese Qingnian Trading Company, and the business is very developed. Therefore, the Dutch Philips Bulb Company in the area is very jealous and has repeatedly tried to slander and hinder its sales. In February of this year, they used the excuse that the Half Bulb was their patent and filed a lawsuit with the local Dutch government, ordering the Aiboer sales office to stop selling. Because the area is completely within the Dutch sphere of influence, the Dutch can do whatever they want. The Aiboer Half Bulb was sacrificed to this evil force. Recently, the Philips Company in the area felt that among the thirty or so types of light bulbs sold in Java, the Aiboer long filament electric light bulb was still a strong competitor to the company in terms of quality. Therefore, they did not hesitate to twist the facts and even claimed that the extremely common glass tube evacuation method in the world was patented by the company. They again filed a lawsuit with the local government, prohibiting the sale of Aiboer light bulbs in the area and demanding compensation for losses. In addition to hiring lawyers to defend themselves in court, the Aiboer sales office also telegraphed the Aiboer headquarters for instructions. The Aiboer headquarters has now requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate on the basis of reason and law, and has also requested assistance from various powerful groups. Famous groups in Shanghai, such as the Citizens' National Goods Promotion Association, the Chinese National Goods Maintenance Association, and the National Goods Factory Federation, are all very indignant at the Dutch Philips' unreasonable rejection of Chinese goods. It is a small matter that the Aiboer Company loses a part of its business, but it greatly affects the overseas trade of all national goods. Therefore, a large-scale joint meeting will soon be held to decide on effective countermeasures.

San You Factory Workers Petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau Yesterday 189

Due to a factory closure issue, a dispute arose at the San You Industrial Company's main factory in Yinxiang Port, Hudong. The authorities intervened several times, and the factory temporarily maintained the workers' meals, and the labor side was notified to await resolution. Due to the large number of people, they spread throughout the bureau's courtyard, auditorium, and stairs. The workers were quite orderly, and the bureau police did not interfere. A practical solution would be determined within two weeks. The factory's shortfall in meal expenses could be notified by the bureau to be paid in full according to the original amount. The workers were also instructed that for future matters, representatives could be sent to negotiate, rather than the entire group coming to the bureau, to avoid causing misunderstandings. Local News 2

Yu Tang Township Holds Cooperative Rice Seedling Planting 190

Cooperative rice seedling planting, also known as public rice seedling planting, is an organization formed by farmers working together. It is not only convenient for pest control but also saves economic and labor resources. It is extremely important for improving rice cultivation. However, as this is an innovative initiative, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Industry has compiled a general overview of cooperative rice seedling planting and selected the Shanghai Yu Tang Township Model Agricultural Extension Area to hold a demonstration for farmers to emulate. The Provincial First Agricultural Experiment Field Songjiang Branch was instructed to send personnel to work with the area's instructor, Zhang Weibin, to provide guidance before the planting season this year. Following the regulations in the overview of cooperative rice seedling planting, village heads and deputies from nearby villages were convened to discuss implementation. A total of five cooperative rice seedling planting areas were established, with 17 participating farmers, including Chen Ziyu and others. The rice seedling field area was 17.3 mu, with varieties including Quyü and four others. The seed quantity was 23 shi and 8 dou. The seed soaking period was from April 30th to May 4th, the sowing period was from May 4th to 9th, the number of egg collections was two to four times, the number of moth traps was three to six times, and the transplanting date was from May 20th to June 1st. The results were good. The details have been reported to the Department of Industry for record. Yesterday, the department instructed the field to continue promoting it to benefit people's livelihoods.

Noteworthy Suicide Incident of a Poor Person 191

▲Wife About to Give Birth, Utterly Penniless

▲Father Unsympathetic, Taking All Savings

▲Yu Guihua Pawned Clothes to Buy Opium

▲Departing the World of Suffering

Yu Guihua, a Zhenjiang native who previously ran a paper box workshop on Zhoujiazui Road in Hongkou, was 26 years old. After his business failed and the paper box workshop closed, he moved to live upstairs in the Zhenhua Wine Shop on Dongyouheng Road. Although he repeatedly asked people to find him a job, he was unsuccessful, leading to extreme financial hardship. Yu then instructed his wife to work as a female worker at the nearby Changxin Tobacco Company, relying on her meager daily income to make ends meet. Recently, his wife became pregnant and was about to give birth. To maintain their daily lives, she had to go to the factory to work every day. The factory owner, seeing her plight, gave Yu's wife five yuan as expenses for childbirth. However, after several days of household expenses, only one yuan and eight jiao remained. The day before yesterday afternoon, Yu Guihua's father, Changgen, came from Zhabei to his son's place to ask for pocket money. His son told him about their financial difficulties, but his father did not believe him. Guihua then gave him one yuan and said that he had eight jiao left and needed to keep it for household expenses. His father refused and then took another six jiao. Changgen still ignored him. In the end, Guihua gave his father all one yuan and eight jiao, which finally resolved the matter. After Changgen left, Guihua's resentment grew. He pawned his only cloth robe, bought opium, and returned home. After his wife fell asleep, he secretly swallowed it and committed suicide. When his wife discovered it at around 7:00 AM yesterday morning, he was already unconscious. She urgently arranged for a car to take him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Unfortunately, he had taken the poison for too long and died on the way.
