Li Zhong Lane Responsibility Issue for Indian Policeman's Killing 196

The case of an Indian policeman committing murder and stabbing a tenant in Li Zhong Lane, Yuezhou Road, on the 2nd of this month has attracted considerable attention from all sectors. However, there are various rumors and disagreements regarding the nature of the housing and the employment of the Indian policeman. The following is a record of the statement from the He Xing Real Estate Company, the owner of Li Zhong Lane, regarding this case: (1) The entire real estate of Li Zhong Lane is mortgaged to the China Business Company for 126,000 taels of silver. The contract stipulates that the rent will be used as interest. The right to collect rent and hire gatekeepers rests with the China Business Company. (2) Tenants are in arrears of a large amount of rent, averaging eight or nine months per household, which is a fact. However, the rent arrears are unrelated to the Indian policeman incident, as the court handles issues such as rent arrears and evictions, and the bailiffs execute them. (3) The houses in Li Zhong Lane are the property of He Xing Real Estate Company and are purely jointly owned, not owned by Chen Changkun personally. Due to the mortgage conditions, the China Business Company manages the company's rental gatekeeping. The internal administration is the responsibility of Ling Yongde, the company's manager. (4) The responsibility for the Indian policeman's murder case lies with the China Business Company. The He Xing Real Estate Company has no right to interfere due to the mortgage contract.

Reaction to the British American Tobacco Factory's Promulgation of Management Rules 197

▲Fifth District Cigarette Industry Union Holds Meeting to Discuss

Since the authorities of the British American Tobacco Factory in Pudong suddenly promulgated 23 management rules on the 1st of last month, the workers believe that the implementation of these harsh rules has made the workers in the factory unable to laugh or cry, and their actions are restricted at every step. The most severe of these include the fact that workers are not allowed to take leave, and the factory can arbitrarily dismiss workers. This has caused a unanimous and violent reaction. The Fifth District Cigarette Industry Union believes that the rules promulgated by the factory not only favor the interests of the capital side but also contradict the conditions of labor-capital cooperation and the factory's existing customs. If strict resistance is not taken, the workers' inherent rights will be completely exploited by the factory. Therefore, at 6:00 PM the day before yesterday, an emergency representative assembly was convened to discuss countermeasures. More than 100 representatives attended. Zhong Quan, representative of the City Party Headquarters, and Tan Peiyan, representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, attended to provide guidance. The presidium of Gu Ruofeng, Fei Keguang, and Pan Quanrong was elected, and Sun Xiaozhu recorded the meeting. After the meeting began as scheduled, the harsh rules promulgated by the factory were discussed. All representatives believed that since the government has promulgated factory regulations, they should be fully implemented. Now, the factory adopts the factory regulations that are beneficial to the factory and incorporates them into the management rules. It only favors the interests of the capital side. Furthermore, after carefully reading the articles, they found that they contradicted the labor-capital cooperation contract signed in the 17th year of the Republic and the existing customs. The factory is intentionally disrupting the regulations and destroying the conditions. It was decided: (1) to submit a request to a higher level to promptly revise the rules; (2) in the name of the representative assembly, to notify the factory that the management rules should be suspended until the higher level has revised them; otherwise, the factory will be responsible for any accidents that occur. There was also detailed discussion on the factory's refusal to allow workers to take leave and the deduction of rice subsidies. The meeting did not adjourn until late at 10:00 PM.

Robber Who Opened Fire to Resist Arrest Awaits Sentencing 201

Li Jinsheng, a robber from Yangzhou, was charged with robbing the Huayang Printing House at 824 Wuchang Road of 520 yuan, 9 jiao, and 6 fen, and a silver watch at midnight on May 31st, with accomplices. The neighbors He Ji Clothing Store apprentice Zhou Wenhua saw them fleeing and chased after them, blowing the alarm. The nearby Hua police officer number 3072 heard the alarm and rushed to the scene. The robber Li dared to open fire to resist arrest, penetrating the police officer's uniform. Fortunately, it did not penetrate the flesh. The officer then returned fire, shooting Li in the leg, causing him to fall to the ground. He was immediately searched and 106 yuan, 7 jiao, and a silver watch were confiscated. He was detained and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation. He denied opening fire to resist arrest and was ordered to be detained for further investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong held a continued trial. The police lawyer stated that in the adjournment period, the bullet casings found at the scene had been verified and matched the bullets from the handgun seized from the defendant. The handgun and bullets were presented for inspection. Hua police officer 3072 testified that the defendant fired three shots, breaking his uniform and holster, and was lucky not to have been hit. The defendant confessed that a certain Li who was on the run had proposed that they go rob, but the shots fired at the time were fired into the sky to warn off pursuers and he did not dare to shoot at the police. He pleaded for leniency. Judge Shen, after appointing a pro bono lawyer to defend the defendant in court, ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody for sentencing on a scheduled date.

Mother Does Not Know Her Own Children's Names 202

▲Child Trafficking Case Cracked on Qiongzhou Ship

Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang, investigators from the Chinese Women and Children Relief Association, inspected the Xiamen-bound Qiongzhou ship docked at the Taikoo Wharf in the French Concession at 11:30 yesterday morning. They saw a middle-aged woman in the steerage cabin carrying two boys, one large and one small, whose behavior was suspicious. They questioned her in detail. The woman claimed that her surname was Lu Lin, she was 38 years old, a local, and the two children were her own. She said they were going to Hong Kong, etc. When asked for the names of her two children, she was speechless. When the two children were questioned, Chen and others thought, "How can a mother not know her own children's names?" Clearly, there was something else going on. The woman, seeing that she had been exposed, claimed that the two children had been sold to her by a friend. The older child was five years old, sold for 75 yuan, and she had already paid 15 yuan. The younger child was two years old, sold for 40 yuan, and she had already paid 10 yuan. She said that after she went to Hong Kong and returned, she would pay the rest. The two investigators became even more suspicious upon hearing this and questioned them separately. The woman finally revealed the truth, claiming that an unknown Wuxi woman had entrusted her to take the two children to Xiamen to sell. The older child could be sold for 200 yuan, and the younger child could be sold for 150 yuan, etc. Chen and others, seeing that the case was clear, took the three of them to the customs water police station. After the police chief clarified the situation, he deemed that the woman was trafficking children for export, separating families, which was a heinous crime. He sent detectives Huang Songsheng, along with the two investigators Chen and Lin, to send them to the local court for sentencing.

They also rescued the trafficked boys Liu Dexiao, 13, Fan Ayou, 5, and the girl Mei Xiuying, 8. They were taken to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. First, police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that he was accusing the defendants of violating Article 257 of the Criminal Law, obstructing marriage and family, and presented the details of the case, requesting an adjournment. Then, the 13-year-old boy Liu Dexiao testified that he was from Jiangyin, his mother had died, and only his father remained in his hometown. He came to Shanghai with a fellow villager ten days ago and got lost on the way. Because he was alone, he stayed in the alleys at night and joined the beggars at the bridges during the day, helping them pull carts. A few days ago, the defendant Wang Gensheng took him to the hotel, etc. Wang Gensheng confessed that Mei Xiuying was brought by Zhang Gensheng and he spent 25 yuan to buy her as his adopted daughter. He found Liu Dexiao with the beggars, rescued him, and took him to the hotel, preparing to take him back to the countryside and have him farm. He was not selling him. Chen Yongcai testified that the 5-year-old boy Fan Ayou was bought from the countryside by Yang Zhiquan, who brought him to the hotel and asked him to take care of him. Fan Chen testified that she was in Shanshi and recently received a letter from Chen Yongcai, so she came to Shanghai to help take care of the children at the hotel. Wang Chen testified that she had recently become acquainted with Wang Gensheng and did not know about the trafficked children. After Judge Ge Cixun verified the confessions, he ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody separately for another hearing in seven days. The three children were temporarily sent to the Jiliang Institute and the Women and Children Relief Association for care.

Huaiyin Lane Property Dispute Case, Original Plaintiff's Appeal Rejected 204

Wang Qinglin, the owner of Huaiyin Lane on Zhejiang Road in the British Concession, mortgaged the property to the China Land Reclamation Bank for 150,000 taels of silver last year. His cousin Wang Xichang learned of this and filed a lawsuit with the First Special Court, demanding an analysis because the property deed's household name was Wang Bingji, which was originally co-owned by his grandfather Bingchun and Qinglin's father Bingkun. The first instance ruled against the plaintiff, and Xichang appealed to the Second High Court Branch. Judge Hu Yigu summoned the appellant, who presented his appeal, stating that the current photo of the deed had been changed to Wang Bingkun's household name, which was forged. The signature on the distribution agreement in the 25th year of Guangxu did not match his father's signature on the consent form. The original judgment also recognized that Huaiyin Lane was not the Hu family's residence and was not subject to the distribution agreement, etc. Judge Hu then asked the appellant if he was an adopted son, when his father died, and if he had ever received a share of the rent from the Huaiyin Lane houses. The appellant replied that he was an adopted son, his father died in the first year of the Republic, and he had never received a share of the rent from Huaiyin Lane. The respondent's agent, lawyer Zhu Xiyun, replied that the deed's household name was Wang Bingkun, which was the respondent's father's name, and the original deed could be checked. The original signature on the case matched the distribution agreement. The Shanghai Municipal Police Department had certified that Huaiyin Lane was not formerly known as the Hu family's residence. As for starting to inherit property, it had been 75 years. Furthermore, the appellant's grandfather and the respondent's father had already divided the inheritance in the 7th year of Xianfeng. If the property was not included in the distribution, why did the appellant's father not claim co-ownership when he received 5,000 yuan in the 25th year of Guangxu? The appellant was already an adult when his father died. Why did he only claim rights 21 years later? The statute of limitations had long expired. The appellant was being used by others to claim co-ownership, and the purpose was extortion. The appeal should be rejected. The closing arguments were immediately declared. The appellant's agent, lawyer Mei Hezhang, filed a motion, citing Article 201 of the Code of Civil Procedure, requesting the court to reopen the arguments, stating that there was new evidence that had not been presented. He said that the appellant had suffered three nervous breakdowns since the interrogation and had attempted suicide. Could a settlement be continued? Judge Hu opened a hearing a few days ago to ask if the two parties had conducted a settlement. Lawyer Zhu Xiyun replied that the appellant was being foolishly used by others to attempt to divide the property, making it difficult to reach a settlement. Judge Hu then instructed the appellant's wife that the customs of Shanghai society had recently been poor, and some people often sow discord, provoke litigation, and profit from it. Unwise people are often fooled without realizing it. The appeal in this case was unreasonable. Therefore, the motion to reopen the arguments was denied, and the appellant's appeal was rejected in court.

Rice Merchants Association Clarifies that Shu Zhanyuan Does Not Sell Japanese Rice 205

On August 2nd, the Rice Merchants Association received a letter from a named Civil Federation, with a "Formosa News" paper dated August 1st attached. The paper contained a section that claimed there was a corrupt merchant in the rice industry, stating that Shu Zhanyuan, the manager of Rintai San Rice Firm, and Rintai Company, Santai, Kaitai, Jitaishan, and other rice firms, sold enemy goods rice. After receiving the letter, the association, with the anti-Japanese movement being intensified, believed that such a record should be strictly investigated. It immediately publicly elected two standing committee members, Shi and Zhang, to go to the rice firms for detailed investigations. At the same time, it received a letter from Shu Zhanyuan, the manager of the rice firms, with a "Formosa News" paper attached, requesting a detailed investigation to clarify the facts. Shi and Zhang went to various rice firms such as Rintai Company and Kaitai Santai to conduct detailed investigations of various account books and found no evidence of selling rice from Japanese merchants. They then went to Rintai San Rice Firm, which was related to the rice firms, and repeatedly checked the account books, also finding no facts as reported. They reported back to the association after completing the investigation. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, a full executive committee meeting was convened to discuss the matter. Executive committee members Lu Wenshao, Shi Hongxun, Zhang Nianyi, Qu Zhenhua, Wang Weiquan, Zhang Heming, Lu Guishan, Huang Gengbo, representative Xu Zhenyue, and more than ten others attended. First, Shi and Zhang reported on their detailed investigations of Rintai Company, Santai Kaitai, and other rice firms, stating that the firms had no transactions with Japanese merchants or sales of rice. The account books of Rintai San Rice Firm, which was related to the rice firms, were also repeatedly checked, and there were no facts as reported. They asked for discussion. Next, Shu Zhanyuan, the manager of the rice firms, was also present and claimed that the "Formosa News" reported that he, Shu Zhanyuan, the manager of Rintai and other rice firms, sold rice from Japanese merchants, which was completely baseless. If there were such facts, he would accept extremely severe punishment. If there were no such facts, the report damaged his reputation. In addition to directly contacting the newspaper to negotiate, he asked for justice. It was decided that the association would publish a cover advertisement in various newspapers to prove that the rice firms did not sell rice from Japanese merchants and to notify all sectors to avoid misunderstandings. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Ministry of Industry Denies Interest-Bearing Loan of American Cotton 207

Investigation of Jiangsu Province's Industries by the Ministry of Industry 208

▲ Compiling a National Gazetteer of Provincial Industries

Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo, due to the lack of systematic reports and materials on the industrial situation of various provinces in the country that could be relied upon, specifically drafted a plan to compile a national industrial gazetteer. He instructed the Bureau of International Trade to take charge of the matter. The director of the bureau, He Bingxian, has been actively proceeding with the plan in recent days. Zhu Xinong and Ruan Jing have been appointed as the chief and deputy editors, respectively, and Hou Houpei as the director of investigation. Other personnel have also been appointed and have begun their work, starting with an investigation of Jiangsu. According to sources within the bureau, the goal of this investigation is solely to promote industry and develop trade. The materials collected will be provided as a reference for industrialists and entrepreneurs. Our country has a great abundance of fine industrial raw materials and various products, but due to a lack of understanding of the true situation, they cannot be utilized. As a result, the treasures bestowed by nature are left unused, while daily necessities are supplied by foreigners. The annual leakage of wealth amounts to tens of millions, which is due to the weakness of domestic industries and the opportunity seized by foreign goods. The key to developing resources and promoting industry lies in having a full understanding of the industrial situation in various regions. Only then can one follow the map and design development plans. The importance of this work is evident, especially at a time when promoting national goods is being advocated. It is even more important to understand the situation of domestically produced goods. It has now been decided that, in addition to Jiangsu, provinces such as Zhejiang should also be actively investigated. It is estimated that Jiangsu province can be completed within four months. The bureau's appointed investigators, numbering over ten, will soon set off in different directions to conduct on-site investigations in various counties.

Letter from the National Construction Commission to the Municipal Government Praising Electrical Companies in the War Zone 209

During the war, the electrical companies in the war zone of this city勉力continued to operate勉力, resulting in significant losses. The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities submitted the company's losses to the Municipal Government for transmission to the National Construction Commission for record-keeping. The National Construction Commission has now replied to the Municipal Government, stating that commendation should be granted. The Municipal Government has instructed the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities yesterday to issue a commendation. The full text is recorded below as an instruction:

Regarding the matter, according to the National Construction Commission's letter No. 210, "We received your government's letter No. 224, stating that the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities has reported on the impact of the Shanghai Incident on the city's electrical companies, requesting review and verification, and attaching a list of losses for each electrical company. After investigation, the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company and the Zhenru Electrical Company were able to maintain power supply to the rear during the most intense period of the war, which is commendable. Your government should issue a commendation to encourage them. As for the post-war arrangements for each company and how to assist them in resuming operations, it is assumed that your government has already made considerable preparations, and we hope you will provide a reply." This case was previously submitted to the government by the bureau, along with a list of losses for each electrical company in the city, and a reply was sent as requested, along with instructions to notify them. In accordance with the aforementioned letter, the bureau is hereby instructed to follow the instructions and issue a commendation, and to submit the companies' plans and the bureau's plans to assist the companies in resuming operations for review and approval. This order.

Conviction of Male and Female Kidnappers 215

▲ Li Acai Sentenced to Four Years of Imprisonment

The rogue Ningbo native Li Acai, on June 2nd, colluded with his adopted mother Qiao Cao to abduct A'liu, the daughter of Zhang Feng of Ruifu Lane No. 42, and entrusted her to Yang A'quan, who was at large, to take her to Pudong with the intention of selling her. The French Concession Police Detective Ding Wensheng and others discovered this and arrested Li and Cao, rescued the girl, and brought her back to the police station. Later, it was discovered that Li had also abducted his adopted brother's wife, Ding Zhenzhu, to Songjiang, where she was introduced by Jin Genfa and sold to Wu Xinzhai as his wife, receiving eighty yuan in profit. In addition, in the third and fourth months of the year, he abducted two girls on the road and entrusted them to Cai Wu and others for sale. Therefore, Detective Ding went to Songjiang and arrested Jin and Wu, rescued the girl Zhenzhu, and brought them to Shanghai. Zhenzhu was first handed over to her family to be taken back. Subsequently, related persons Cai Wu, Cai Jinsong, Gao Shouguan, Zhu Yu, Zhang Wu, etc., were also arrested. However, the other two girls had already been sold and could not be retrieved. Li and others were then handed over to the Second Special Court and prosecuted under Article 257 of the Criminal Code. After repeated trials by Judge Li Changnian, he declared the conclusion of the debate. Yesterday, Judge Li took the seat in the First Criminal Court and sentenced Li Acai to three counts of abducting women under the age of twenty with the intention of profiting, each carrying a sentence of three years of imprisonment. He was also sentenced to one year of imprisonment for abducting a woman under the age of twenty, depriving her of the right to parental authority, and the sentence will be executed for four years of imprisonment. Qiao Cao was sentenced to one year of imprisonment for abducting a woman under the age of twenty, depriving her of the right to parental authority. Cai Wu was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for abducting a woman under the age of twenty with the intention of profiting. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be credited. Jin Genfa, Wu Xinzhai, Cai Jinsong, Gao Shouguan, Zhu Yu, and Zhang Wu were all found not guilty.

Weather Report 231

The meteorological forecast from the Xujiahui Observatory at 4:30 PM yesterday said that the Shandong coast was clear, with no wind direction. The Yangtze River basin and coastal areas were hot and cloudy, with wind from the southeast to southwest. There was thunder in this port. There was a hurricane in the Pacific Ocean, west of Guam, which was moving northwest. As for the hurricane blowing towards the Sea of Japan, its center had advanced to within 120 miles of the intersection of 42 degrees north latitude and 135 degrees east longitude at noon, and the wind force was unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 99.3 and the lowest was 73.9. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 95.0 and the lowest was 77.2.

Questioning Mr. Xu Jiqing's Article (Respectfully Addressed to Those Who Doubt the Abolition of Taels and the Adoption of the Yuan) by Li·Xi·Yuan· 232

Recently, various sectors have expressed their opinions on the issue of abolishing taels and adopting the yuan, gathering wisdom and benefiting widely, which is a great event. Yesterday, Mr. Xu Jiqing published an article entitled "(Respectfully Addressed to Those Who Doubt the Abolition of Taels and the Adoption of the Yuan)," explaining the four prerequisite issues advocated by various sectors recently, enlightening and inspiring, with painstaking efforts. However, I am not talented and still have many points in Mr. Xu's statement that I cannot understand. I will briefly state my humble opinions, hoping that Mr. Xu can further educate me.

(1) Regarding how to stipulate the legal tender value, Mr. Xu said, "For each silver yuan, the standard should be the pure silver it contains, and then add the actual minting cost based on the amount of pure silver, which will be the future legal tender value," etc. If this refers specifically to the new silver coins minted in the future, my ideal is naturally like this, and it seems unnecessary for Mr. Xu to explain. If it refers to the silver coins currently circulating in various regions, there are more than twenty types, with varying amounts of pure silver and different minting costs. In that case, what should be used as the standard for setting the legal tender value, and how should it be stipulated? Mr. Xu has not explained any of this, which shows that it is necessary to gather all parties and deliberate calmly before the event, and that the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan cannot be carried out rashly. (2) Regarding the issue of issuance reserves, Mr. Xu cited the Bank of China as an example, believing that the issuance of banknotes by the Bank of China, etc., has already been implemented publicly and there is no need to doubt it. However, based on the facts, I feel that Mr. Xu's statement is slightly inconsistent with logic. The so-called "taels" in the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan refer to various silver taels throughout the country, not just the standard yuan. Even if the banks in Shanghai alone can achieve public issuance with sufficient reserves, how should the issuance of banknotes in various localities be managed and supervised after the abolition of silver taels throughout the country? Mr. Xu did not mention how to prepare for this in advance. To generalize from one corner to the whole country seems arbitrary. Moreover, the issuance system discussed by people at the time refers to national banks. Currently, there are no fewer than dozens of domestic and foreign banks with the right to issue banknotes in the country. How can one Bank of China represent the whole? Even taking the Bank of China as an example, according to its 20th-year report, the amount of issuance reached 190 million, while Mr. Xu's so-called public inspection only covers 90 million in the Shanghai warehouse. The remaining 100 million issued by branches in the north and south have not been made public. To use a part to represent the whole, how is that possible? It is said that Mr. Xu is one of the directors of the Bank of China, perhaps intending to plan a further step at this time to seek full public issuance? This is what I am optimistic about. Furthermore, regarding the 90 million that Mr. Xu claims is currently public, 40% is guaranteed as reserve. After the September 18th Incident last year, it was suddenly announced that all of it would be replaced, and all domestic bonds were replaced with Japanese and American bonds, and title deeds, etc. Considering the meaning of complete independence of issuance, where were these securities withdrawn from, and where were they exchanged? If it is said that they were bought and sold on the market, then why is there no news of such a large transaction among foreigners, and what kind of reserves were used to compensate for the losses incurred? All of this is what outsiders are eager to understand and should be generously announced by those who advocate publicity. Furthermore, the issuance amounts of various private banks in our country are unlimited, which is criticized by commentators. Taking the Bank of China as an example, with a capital of 25 million yuan, although official shares account for one-fifth, it is essentially a private joint-stock company, not established by the whole people or the state. The current issuance of banknotes exceeds eight times the capital, which cannot be said to be a malformed issuance system in our country. At this time, the wise men's advocacy of abolishing taels must first be thoroughly rectified and reformed, which seems to be insightful. Mr. Xu, who is as knowledgeable as you, should also have the same feeling. (3) Mr. Xu said, "Banknotes should be based on convertibility. How can soft currency be issued without hard currency as a reserve?" etc. Regardless of the distinction between convertible and non-convertible banknotes in monetary theory, it is also difficult to explain based on the situation in our country. Are Fengchao and Jinchao not banknotes? Why can't they be converted? Are Pingchao and Hanchao not banknotes? Why should they be recovered with public bonds worth only 20% of their value? What I am worried about is precisely this. (4) Mr. Xu said that the suspension of convertibility of Pinghan was a temporary chaotic order. Even if an evil government were to change, regardless of whether taels are abolished or yuan are adopted, there is a possibility of recurrence at any time, which has nothing to do with the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan, etc. According to commentators, after the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan, the quantity of banknotes will inevitably expand, and circulation will inevitably become wider. If the issuance system is not fundamentally rectified in advance, once misfortune occurs and the same mistakes are repeated, the disaster will be a hundred or a thousand times greater than that of the former Pinghan, which can be asserted. Who says it has nothing to do with the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan? (5) Regarding the concentration of cash by the Wuhan government in the past, I also cannot help but doubt it. Even under the so-called "chaotic order" by Mr. Xu at that time, why could the banknotes with the Hankou imprints of Siming, Zhongnan, Xingye, Guangdong, and other banks still be fully converted in Hankou, while the Hankou banknotes of the Bank of China were only recovered at a discount of 20%, and then they colluded with the government to exchange them for long-term, low-interest public bonds, and then changed the banknotes issued in Hankou to those with the Shanghai imprint, and fully used them. This kind of issuing system with a changed face must be thoroughly reformed before the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan, so as to avoid one mistake leading to another. This is almost a certain fact, and Mr. Xu is wise, and I think he thinks so too. Furthermore, I cannot help but say that recently, a few financiers and scholars have been vigorously guaranteeing that the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan will have a hundred benefits and not a single drawback, and that it can be implemented immediately. The situation is very similar to that of vigorously guaranteeing the credit of domestic debt a year ago and inducing people to invest. Recalling that at that time, a few bankers and scholars repeatedly promoted how reliable the domestic debt fund was, how sufficient the tax revenue was, and how strict the supervision of various groups was, writing articles and publishing pamphlets, on the one hand, they indulged the government's expansion of domestic debt issuance, and on the other hand, they aroused the people's interest in investment. When the time changed, a few bankers, who got the news first, sold off one after another, and then issued the argument that domestic debt was unbearable, telling people that the guarantee reserves for their domestic debt had been withdrawn and replaced with foreign securities such as Japanese, British, and American securities, and title deeds, etc., complacent. However, tens of millions of domestic debt holders have filled the ditches and cannot extricate themselves. Learning from the past and being cautious for the future, I cannot help but be suspicious and fearful of those who are now arguing and defending the immediate abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan. Mr. Xu has been advocating the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan for fifteen years. He must have tasted all the hardships in this process. Why could it not be realized slowly in the past, and why can it be implemented immediately today? What is the progress between now and then? My foolishness is what I have not understood, and I deeply hope that Mr. Xu can enlighten me.

Supplement to the Local Edition of Shen Bao

Words

Wang Geng Sentenced to Imprisonment 234

— Fo

During the Shanghai War, Wang Geng, the former independent brigade commander of the 88th Division, left his post without permission and entered the enemy's key area. He was detained by the Japanese army and released after negotiations. The military headquarters and military law department organized a high-level military law review and thorough investigation. It was confirmed that there was no suspicion or evidence of communication with the enemy, and he was sentenced to only two years and six months of imprisonment.

The new criminal law now imitates Europe and the United States, focusing on evidence, which is not bad. However, in China, before all investigation agencies and detective techniques have been established, whether it is applicable to focus solely on evidence is a question. Moreover, Wang Geng's case was during a military period, and whether it is applicable to ordinary criminal procedures is also a question. For the time being, I will not discuss this. Since the authorities have organized a high-level military law review, reviewed it several times, and thoroughly investigated it, they believe that there is no suspicion or evidence of communication with the enemy, but I say that evidence may be absent, but if you say there is no suspicion, then I dare not believe it.

The 19th Route Army fought against the enemy for more than a month. The center of the war was in Jiangwan, Baziqiao, and Yunzaobang. After Wang Geng was captured by the enemy, the Japanese army suddenly changed its battle plan and focused on the Liuhong area, which led to a sudden change in the situation of our army. This is suspicious point one.

Wang Geng, as a military commander, ran into the enemy's key area for no reason when the war situation between the two armies was serious, which not only damaged the dignity of our army, but also lost his personal character. What was the purpose of Wang's trip? This is suspicious point two.

Wang Geng was detained by the enemy, and the enemy must have regarded him as a rare commodity and would not let him go easily. Try reading the enemy's war pictorials. Wang Geng's head was drooping and his face was lost when he was severely questioned at the enemy headquarters. Everyone who saw it thought it was a great shame. Why was he released immediately after negotiations? The enemy kept Wang's confession strictly confidential and did not announce it. What method will our side use to investigate? Then, was our military situation leaked? This is another suspicious point three.

Literature and Art

Lament of Poverty and Illness 235

— Yun Jian Gong Xia

The ancients said that poverty is not the source of illness, but poverty is often adjacent to illness. When illness comes, you can still find medicine, but when poverty comes, there is nowhere to find gold and silver. Knowing that you should be cautious about illness so that there is no illness, but unwilling to be content with poverty, you become more and more poor. I am not afraid of poverty, but only afraid of illness. I only ask that the illness subside and I will be an immortal.

Feelings on Seeing Flowers 236

The wind and rain have destroyed the luxuriant flowers in the pond, leaning on the railing and feeling a thousand emotions. Knowing that she is beautiful because of many tribulations, bidding farewell to drifting and sighing forever. Seeing each other for three days, I was startled by the haste, and recalling the past eight years, I hate the endlessness. In a fleeting moment, the spring is old, and I am afraid that it will be difficult to see each other again in this life.

Science

A Brief Discussion on Enamel Products 237

— Shen Min

There are many enamel products, such as washbasins, enamel signs, and cooking pots, all made of enamel. The inventor of enamel was probably Hiokling of England in 1799. However, the cloisonné produced in Peiping, China, was invented as early as the Ming Dynasty, and it really has the same meaning. However, no one used to study and improve it, so it was only used in artworks. However, the base of enamel is made of iron, while the base of cloisonné is made of copper or silver. This is a different characteristic. The method of making enamel is to first make an iron base or a base made of zinc and alloy. However, it cannot contain lead because lead is toxic. If it is made into food utensils, it will be terrible. After the base is made, then apply the enamel solution. This enamel solution is usually divided into two layers. The solution applied to the first layer has a very high melting point, and the attached layer is not uniform and dense, becoming a porous substance. Because the metal of the base has the physical property of expanding when heated and contracting when cooled, it must leave room for expansion and contraction, so it must have pores. The second layer can use a compound that is easier to melt. Its properties are similar to the glaze on porcelain. Now I will briefly list an example of the raw materials and mixing methods used in the two layers.

(1) The first layer of enamel solution. This layer is related to the adhesion of the enamel to the base, so it is very important. The raw materials used must be compatible with the metal of the base. The size of the pores must also match the expansion and contraction degree of the metal used. Usually, twelve parts of silica powder, half a part of borax, and six parts of fluorite are used. After melting the above compounds, add a small amount of ammonium carbonate, alum, and other products.

(2) The second layer of enamel. This layer is related to the color and beauty of the product, so it cannot be ignored. The raw materials commonly used for mixing are 32 parts of feldspar, 22 parts of borax, 7 parts of quartz, 15 parts of Stonnous onide, 8 parts of sodium carbonate, 36 parts of fluorite, and 225 parts of N t e. Then add various pigments to be used. However, pigments are mostly metal compounds, such as Onide of lead, Antinoky inide, and Eobalt Silicate, etc., which are not easily soluble directly, so a mordant must be added. Borax silicate, etc., have the function of mordant.

Now that we know the raw materials and mixing methods of enamel, we have a rough idea. Now let's briefly talk about the working methods. The first part is making the base, which is mostly made by another factory. The enamel factory only does the enamel coating project. The coating project is to first crush the raw materials and melt them separately in a crucible to turn them into a molten solution. Then dip the base in it and stir it evenly. The procedure is not very complicated. The difficult part is whether the proportion of the mixture and the raw materials used are appropriate. Finally, I will introduce a common method for testing the quality of enamel. This method is to first soak the enamel product in boiling water for a few minutes, and then put it in ice for a few minutes. Repeat this two or three times, or several times. If there are no cracks on the surface, it is good. Otherwise, it is bad. If you want to know whether there is lead in the base of the product, you can use an egg, break it, mix the yolk and white evenly, and pour it into the enamel container. Let it stand for a day and a night. If there is lead, it will be found to be black, because there is sulfur in the egg yolk.

Social Improvement Discussion Association

Contribution on Children's Toys 238

— Cang Ping

Because I am a young man who has just left childhood, regarding the suggestions for children's toys, I have come up with such a self-righteous contribution based on my own association, for everyone's discussion.

Each child has his own personality. Parents should first understand the child's personality, and then give him toys, which will be more interesting and more beneficial to his intellect. Therefore, children's toys do not have to be fixed on a large scale to be considered beneficial toys.

According to the child's psychology, most children are active, but there are also children who are not active due to congenital deficiencies and monotonous environments. Then, giving active children those large-scale toys will inevitably turn into barbaric activity. The child's physique and bones have not yet fully developed. If they are allowed to be barbaric all their lives, it will not be good for their health. I think the most appropriate compromise is:

For active children, in addition to dynamic toys, give them some static toys. The so-called static toys, such as small sketching boxes, small literary works, small colored picture cards, and similar interesting reading materials for children. It is best to have a small studio in the family, and all the numbers in the study should be manufactured according to the child's physique and psychology, so that the child can rest in this small study when he is not exercising, read books at will, and happily write sketches. In this way, it is really a way to integrate education into games.

For children who are not active, mostly because of physical weakness or monotonous environment, they cannot raise the interest in moving. Parents should try to introduce several neighboring children to the children, buy some sweets to maintain the relationship between the children, and buy a ball to arouse the children's enthusiasm. In this way, those who are not active will naturally become active. If the family is wider, it is best to open up a small garden and provide small hoes and small iron shovels for the children to plant some flowers and plants themselves, and for the children to raise some creatures themselves. Tame dogs and cats are all excellent toys for children, and in addition to playing, they can also learn about the evolution of nature and the healthy virtue of caring for creatures... These are my contributions, and I hope that my colleagues will correct me.

—

Mr. Cheng Peng does not approve of wearing a student uniform on the upper body and shorts on the lower body. He thinks

(A) It is not as beautiful as a suit because it looks like a servant.

My opinion is that it looks ugly, but it is only because it is not common. As for those who laugh at people as servants, they are fundamentally rude themselves; and that person's vision is narrow, which can also be seen.

If it can be implemented uniformly, then it will be the same as foreigners wearing suits. What's so funny? Wearing shorts is certainly cooler. If there is a more comfortable way, not implementing it would be foolish, right? The British also wear shorts. I wonder what Mr. Cheng Peng thinks? Do you say it's not beautiful? That's too much attention to decoration. Do you say it's not dignified? They also wear shorts to pay homage to the emperor, or maybe they are barbarians and have no dignity?

Mr. Cheng said that European and American workers and peasants all wear suits, which I also know, but it is the same as Chinese workers and peasants wearing Chinese short shirts and trousers. They have their customs and habits, which are fundamentally different from ours. If we wear suits, we must follow their etiquette and customs, but I am still Chinese! Otherwise, what should I do?

Mr. Cheng said that suits are economical, but please inquire about the price of handwork. With two sets of cloth suits, although you can avoid being a servant, you still can't see people, because cloth suits will change shape after wearing them for a day or two and must be ironed. Most people don't know how to iron, so... To be done once and for all, and to want to see people, you must use fine呢 or嗶嘰,羽紗.

If there is a social gathering, then formal wear is a must, otherwise foreigners will shake their heads when they see it.

As for being detrimental to public morals, those who have lascivious thoughts will not be strange if they see more. Seeking Trouble

Miss C's Clever Plan 240

— Ying Dai

Since the slogan of (Freedom of Love) was brought from Western countries to China, the general Chinese people, who have always held the view that men and women should be isolated and never interact with each other until old age, have suddenly changed their concepts; and at the same time, slogans such as (Public Socializing) (Equality between Men and Women) have also gradually spread throughout China. And young people, after reaching a certain age, regard the pursuit of the opposite sex as an urgent task.

However, under the current situation, although the voice of public socializing is spreading everywhere, it is not difficult for men with flexible social skills to find girlfriends, but it is indeed a difficult problem for those with inflexible social skills to find a girlfriend. Under this situation, the general young people with unstable blood, in order to not find friends of the opposite sex, sometimes rack their brains and try to woo women they do not know, which is really extraordinarily pitiful! Asking friends for women's names, seeing women's names in newspapers, and even going to the gatekeepers of girls' schools to copy a few girls' names. When they return to school, they send letters regardless of the consequences. If one letter is not answered, they send two letters. If two letters are not answered, they send three letters... They send them endlessly. It doesn't come to a complete stop until they feel that they have no more interest.

Miss C, she studies at a certain girls' school. Recently, she has also received three love letters in a row. The person who wrote the letter has never even met her, let alone know her name. From this point, we can prove that the reason why he knows Miss C's name is either from a friend or from a newspaper, or perhaps he copied it from the gatekeeper of a certain girls' school.

Miss C is a very mischievous woman. When she received the first letter from the unknown man, she did not reply to him. The second letter was also not replied to. It was not until the third letter that she came up with a clever plan and wrote a reply, inviting him to meet at two o'clock in the afternoon on Sunday at the intersection of Wing On and Sincere, under the iron platform where the red-headed Sikh is directing traffic, for a talk. She also explained that she was wearing a light red cheongsam.

Sunday afternoon arrived. Miss C invited two female friends. After eating, they walked to the main road, stood on the corner of Wing On Company, and looked at the iron platform, but none of the three of them were wearing light red cheongsams. When it was almost two o'clock, a young man in a suit walked excitedly to the iron platform, looking around, as if looking for someone.

He looked for a long time on the sidewalks on both sides of the intersection, but could not find a girl wearing a light red cheongsam. Although there were occasionally women wearing red clothes mixed in among the pedestrians, they did not stop and went their own way, obviously not having any appointments. Finally, in hope, he slowly began to feel disappointed.

He was really anxious to death!

In fact, the person who invited him was on the corner, but he didn't know her. It made them laugh secretly when they saw him in this situation. Later, they walked away, but he didn't leave and was still hoping she would come. But even if he waited until tomorrow, she would not come. He had changed into a new suit for nothing and came to the road to bask in the sun. This is also a kind of reward for those who write blind love letters, right?

Dedicated to my family

Cui Jie's Suicide 241

— Hong

I had a quiet and virtuous cousin. When she was a young lady, her parents truly treasured her like their heart and lungs. Later, she married into a gentry family in the same hometown as a daughter-in-law. Her husband treated her very well, but she had too many young brothers and sisters-in-law. In ordinary days, with many people and mouths, it was not easy

to live. The mother-in-law always protected her children. Even if the daughter-in-law was right, she sometimes had to swallow her anger and put on a smiling face. She had already lived a very wronged life. But fate is coincidental, and misfortunes never come singly. At this time, a gossipy neighbor woman told her that her husband had a mistress in Shanghai and had already forgotten about her. This was originally a joke, but unexpectedly, these few words stirred up a huge wave in her troubled heart. From that day on, her attitude changed drastically. She stayed in her room all day, with no energy at all. Her mother found out and quickly brought her back to live with them. But her nerves had been struck, and she had already begun to suffer from mental illness. When she saw no one around, she would always kneel on the ground and pray, or secretly go to the kitchen to hide the knife. When the family discovered that the kitchen knife was missing, everyone panicked for a while and searched her body and room. Alas... she had already had thoughts of suicide.

One day, her aunt came, and the family naturally had to entertain her well. In the evening, we played mahjong until ten o'clock, and my aunt ordered the old servant woman to accompany her upstairs to sleep. Unexpectedly, at about one o'clock, our front door was knocked as loudly as a continuous drumbeat, making the four of us

jump straight up from our seats. Then there was even more banging…banging…banging…My uncle told the male servant to open the door. Who knew that as soon as the door was opened, a group of bums and hooligans swarmed in, jostling to be first, while shouting, "Your young lady has committed suicide by drowning herself in the West Gate River! Hurry and send someone to identify and claim the body!" ("She's about to die! Should we carry her back?")

When my uncle heard everyone's words, he was so angry that his beard stood on end. He said angrily, "Shut up! Don't talk nonsense! My young lady is sleeping soundly in bed. You must be seeing ghosts!" After saying that, he slammed the door shut. Half an hour later, there was another burst of frantic knocking on the gate, and the noise outside was deafening. Ah! Were they here to report the news again? My aunt was half-doubtful and half-believing at this time, so she quickly moved her lotus steps and went upstairs to see what was going on. As soon as she walked into her daughter's room, she was stunned. It turned out that the bed was empty. She searched under the bed, in the wardrobe, in the corners of the wall, but couldn't even find half a shadow. Only then was she sure that the one who drowned herself must be her A-Cui. She ran downstairs, her face as pale as a ghost, collapsed into a chair, and ordered the people to bring the female corpse back. They heard these words as if they had received a holy decree and left in a gust of wind. In less than a quarter of an hour, the stiff and cold Cui Jie had already appeared before our eyes. Then, the family's wailing and the hooligans' and bums' extortion mixed together into a single sound. Alas... she destroyed herself like this, leaving behind her only three-year-old biological daughter to rely on her frail and elderly grandmother to live her life.

When her husband received this tragic news, he rushed back overnight. He caressed her corpse and wailed loudly, unable to speak through his sobs. Relatives and friends all blamed him, but pitifully, he had no way to defend himself.

Shanghai Local Court 244

▲Criminal Judgments

The court ruled that the two taels of opium paste, for which the prosecutor of this court applied for confiscation due to being ownerless, be confiscated.

▲The Huang Qingyun injury case was dismissed without prosecution.

▲In the Li Xingsheng opium case, Li Xingsheng and Liu Wu-shi were each sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined sixty yuan for jointly intending to profit by providing premises for others to smoke opium. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory enforcement, one yuan will be converted into one day of detention, and two days of detention will offset one day of imprisonment. Zhu A-san was sentenced to one month of imprisonment and fined thirty yuan for smoking opium. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory enforcement, one yuan will be converted into one day of detention, and two days of detention will offset one day of imprisonment. The opium paraphernalia, etc., will be confiscated.

▲The Zhang Haitao case of obstructing freedom and property damage, the appeal was rejected.

▲In the Hu Changhong opium case, Hu Changhong was sentenced to eight months of imprisonment and fined two hundred yuan for intending to sell and possessing opium. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory enforcement, two yuan will be converted into one day of detention, and two days of detention will offset one day of imprisonment. Seventy-six taels of raw opium will be confiscated.

▲In the Zhu Guangzu opium case, Zhu Guangzu was sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined one hundred yuan for intending to sell and possessing opium. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory enforcement, two yuan will be converted into one day of detention, and two days of detention will offset one day of imprisonment. Thirty taels of raw opium will be confiscated.

▲In the Guan Xiao Sanzi opium case, Guan Xiao Sanzi was sentenced to ten months of imprisonment and fined sixty yuan for intending to profit by opening a premises for others to smoke opium. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory enforcement, two yuan will be converted into one day of detention, and two days of detention will offset one day of imprisonment. Opium paraphernalia and red pills, etc., will be confiscated.

▲In the Yang Xiao Sanzi et al. theft case, Yang Xiao Sanzi was sentenced to seven months of imprisonment for committing theft with three or more accomplices during a disaster. Two days of detention will offset one day of imprisonment. The trial of Li Shaozhou is suspended.

▲The Chen Yuanliang et al. injury case.

▲Civil Rulings

▲Zhou Yongmao's request for the Yuyao County Court to assist in the execution: Having reviewed the petition, the Yuyao County Court has remitted three hundred yuan in case funds. You are required to come to the court at 10:00 AM on the 9th of this month to collect the funds first, and the remaining amount will be urged by letter later. This ruling.

▲Tan Shunxing's request for funds: Having reviewed the petition, the debtor in this case has filed a retrial on July 18th. The request to release the case funds will be postponed for discussion. This ruling.

▲Fang Jiawei's petition to seal the property: Having reviewed the petition, the amount of five hundred and eight yuan and sixty-eight cents has been paid by the debtor in installments. You are required to come to the court at 10:00 AM on the 9th of this month to collect the funds. The requested investigation is unnecessary. This ruling.

Zhang. This application for execution: Having reviewed the petition, the case is under appeal, and the requested action should be postponed. This ruling.

▲Cheng Haoliang's request for execution: Having reviewed the petition, the case is under appeal, and the requested action should be postponed. This ruling.

▲Xu Juqing's request for execution: Having reviewed the petition, you are required to await summons. This ruling.

▲Wu Guichan's petition for execution: Having reviewed the petition, permission is granted to summon the case for execution. This ruling.

▲Tang Meiting's continued request for execution: Having reviewed the petition, after the debtor in this case was released on bail by Yao Youli, forty yuan in foreign currency has been paid successively, and the remaining amount is being strictly pursued within a limited time. You are to be notified immediately. This ruling.

▲Bu Wengan's request to close the case: Having reviewed the petition, permission is granted to close the case. Gu Haizhen's petition to close the case: Having reviewed the petition, permission is granted to close the case. This ruling.

▲Zhou Sunshi's petition for strict execution: Having reviewed the petition, permission is granted to continue strict execution. This ruling.

▲Zhang Xiyin's request to collect case funds: Having reviewed the petition, you are required to come to the court at 10:00 AM on the 9th of this month to collect the funds. This ruling. Zhao Zhushi's request for execution: Having reviewed the petition, the case is already under appeal, and the requested action should be postponed. This ruling.

▲Wan Bingwen's petition to detain the case for execution: Having reviewed the petition, the case is already under appeal, and the execution should be postponed. This ruling.

▲Wang Futang's request to collect the Fang receipt: Having reviewed the petition, you are required to bring the receipt to the court at 10:00 AM on the 10th of this month to collect it. This ruling.

▲Hu Mao Gou's request for a ruling on whether to sell the mortgaged real estate: Having reviewed the petition, the mortgaged real estate in this case has been investigated by this court and found that there is no such single household in the cadastral map and household registration. The claim that the real estate has been sold and the price has been paid to the court is a fabrication. This ruling is specifically rejected.

▲Gu Zhongyi's request to seal property for security: Having reviewed the petition, the debtor in this case has already paid one thousand yuan in foreign currency, and the remaining amount is being pursued within a limited time. If the debt is not repaid after the deadline, compulsory execution should be permitted. This ruling.

▲Tong Zhibei, on behalf of his father Tong Yiqun, paid the amount and requested a postponement of installment payments: Having reviewed the petition, after deducting the partial payments received successively, eight hundred yuan in foreign currency is still owed in this case. The debtor should be ordered to comply with the summons to pay the amount in full and not to delay further with excuses, lest it cause inconvenience. Fifty yuan in foreign currency is attached for safekeeping, awaiting collection by the creditor. This ruling.

▲Zhang Baogen's request to guarantee Wu Weishen's submission of receipts: Having reviewed the petition, permission is granted to guarantee. This ruling.

▲Zhang Bofu's request for execution: Having reviewed the petition, you are required to await the summons for execution. This ruling.

▲He Jinlian's petition for the execution of the guarantor: Having reviewed the petition, the guarantor's liability only arises if the principal debtor is actually unable to repay or does not repay the full amount. Since the principal debtor in this case has mortgaged the land receipts, the Baoshan County government has been instructed to seal and auction the land for security, and the petitioner has been notified to go to designate the sealing. It is difficult to predetermine whether it is sufficient to cover the debt, and the immediate request to execute the guarantor is not in accordance with legal procedures and cannot be approved. This ruling.

▲Xie Kang Electrical Materials Store et al.'s request for execution of outstanding payments: Having reviewed the petition, you are required to await the summons for inquiry and verification. The requested donation of detention is temporarily postponed. This ruling.

▲Yang Fusheng's declaration of filing a lawsuit against the execution and requesting a stay of execution: Having reviewed the petition, the requested action is approved. This ruling.

▲Hou Chaoxia submitted the second instance judgment and requested execution: Having reviewed the petition, it is uncertain whether the opposing party has filed a third instance appeal after the second instance judgment. The requested action is temporarily postponed as there is no way to verify before the case file is returned. This ruling.

▲Xu Xiaoyu's petition for execution: Having reviewed the petition, you are required to await the summons for recovery. This ruling.

▲Tao Yaochun's petition for execution: Having reviewed the petition, you are required to await the summons for execution. This ruling.

▲Zhu Gengxin's petition to revoke the provisional attachment: Having reviewed the petition, permission is granted to revoke the provisional attachment. This ruling.

▲Zhu Caihua's petition for execution: Having reviewed the petition, a summons has already been issued for inquiry and recovery. You are to be notified immediately. This ruling.

▲Gao Shouqing's petition for execution: Having reviewed the petition, the case has not yet been finalized, and the requested action is temporarily postponed. This ruling. Xu Xiacun's request to suspend the release of the appraised value of Zhu Maoqing's real estate: Having reviewed the petition, this court auctioned Zhu Maoqing's real estate under the entrustment of the First Special District Local Court, and the proceeds should be sent to the original court for execution. If the petitioner has any claim to the appraised value, they should apply directly to the original court. You are to be notified immediately. This ruling.

▲Gu Junsong's petition to partition property for execution: Having reviewed the petition, a date has already been set for summoning the case for execution, and the will and other supporting documents should be brought to the case for verification. This ruling.

▲Chen Yougen et al.'s petition to release Leng Xianli on bail to await trial outside of custody: Having reviewed the petition, Leng Xianli was turned over to the court by Ma Baiqing, Chen Yurong, etc. The amount of debt claimed is more than ten thousand yuan. The guarantors requested to be released on bail to await trial and are willing to take responsibility for escape, and must have the ability to guarantee. According to the official investigation report, the goods of the three guarantor families are worth approximately five thousand yuan, which is insufficient to guarantee. The requested action cannot be approved. This ruling.

▲Rong Shaoqi and Wu Chuncui requested to withdraw the appeal and retrieve the exhibits submitted to the court: Having reviewed the petition, permission is granted to withdraw the appeal. As for the exhibits submitted to the court, permission is granted to come to the court at 10:00 AM on August 16th to collect them. This ruling.

▲Public Notice of Service

▲In the case of Zhenji Company versus Huang Zhiqing et al. regarding a mortgage loan, the defendant Huang Zhiqing should repay the plaintiff's mortgage loan of 18,500 taels, with 11,000 taels from August 30, 1930, 4,000 taels from December 7, 1930, and 3,500 taels from February 15, 1931, all until the end of execution, and should pay interest at a rate of 1.2% per month. If Huang Zhiqing is unable to repay, the defendants Zhu Ruisheng and Zhu Shaoqin should jointly bear the responsibility for repayment. The litigation costs, excluding the one-quarter withdrawn by the plaintiff, should be borne by the defendant Huang Zhiqing. The defendant Zhu Shaoqin is to be notified.

▲In the case of Guo Binghuai et al. versus Liu Jingqing regarding eviction, the appeal was rejected. The costs of the second instance shall be borne by the appellants themselves. The appellants Guo Binghuai and Hu Ruiyu are to be notified.

▲In the case of Ding Lihong versus Ding Chenshi regarding cohabitation, the defendant should immediately cohabitate with the plaintiff, and the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. The defendant Ding Chenshi is to be notified.
